O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, most dear son, I have completed this book which is the end of the knowledge of medicine along with its fulfillment, and I have made the end through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of the hand, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the work of the hand is neglected in our region and is entirely foreign, thus the knowledge has perished and been destroyed, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in books of the ancients which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this have come errors and vain things, and intentions are closed off and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 Or it seems to me that I wish to vitalize the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will also bring together the forms of the iron tools for cautery, and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has declined.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And he who undertakes it must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that he knows the judgment of members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and the number of veins, and their movement and rest, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	 And because of this, Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and likewise in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things, let him beware lest he fall into error and harm people; as I have seen many times those who engage in this science and then abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 For I saw a foolish physician who cut into an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the artery of the neck; so much blood came out that the woman fell dead at his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 And I saw another physician who removed a stone from a man with water, and the stone was large; so he carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called to extract it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if one cut it out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And I saw another physician who took care of the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the physician, full of ignorance, tightened the break over the wound to the splints with great strength, and left no ointment at all on the wound, and left it so for one term; and he commanded that it should not be loosened; and he remained so that the leg was completely swollen and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come and unbind the leg; and when I had unbound it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 But nevertheless the corruption was already established in the limb, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And a certain other physician drained an abscess which became infected, and then inflamed by the malice of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For a cancer, when it is purged of melancholic humor, one must not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place where all that is corrupt can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: that is to say, the work where there is danger in many situations; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 For which reason it is necessary that you guard yourself, so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you. Therefore, take your weapons in prudence, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised; and leave the terrible diseases for severe sicknesses; and remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on the care of serious illnesses, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and about hot irons, and the chapter is arranged from the head down to the feet; and about the shapes of instruments, and the materials for cautery, and about everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 The second chapter is also about cutting and piercing, and about cupping glasses and wounds, and about extracting arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is arranged about the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and the chapter is arranged from the head down to the feet, and about the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 Just as we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of help and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 Je dis que les qualités de l'aide et du nuisement sont le sujet le plus long et la science la plus subtile et les secrets les mieux répondu ; et à ce propos parlèrent les plus sages, et ils s'accordèrent à cela ; et peu me suffit leurs paroles, car je redoute la longueur.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 Je dis que le cautère est universellement utile pour toutes les complexions qui contiennent de la matière, à l'exception de deux complexions : celles-ci sont une complexion chaude sans matière et une complexion sèche sans matière.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 En complexion chaude et sèche avec matière, certains ont discuté et dit que le cautère est très utile ; les autres ont dit le contraire : que le cautère ne sert à rien pour la maladie qui vient de la chaleur et de la sécheresse.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 Because the nature of fire is so hot, and it should not be used for treating hot diseases with heat or dryness; and he who says otherwise claims that cautery greatly helps hot and dry diseases that come into men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 For when you compare the man's body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 For I have found it to be true by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 And yet, one should not attempt this except for those who have proven it and who know by long experience the chapter on cautery, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the outcomes and duration of time; we do not fear other constitutions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the doctors gathered and agreed on cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of healing, and of greater virtue than burning medical ointment.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 For fire is simple, and does not affect anything but the member that is cauterized, unless it can be named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 Burning medicines spread from one member to another, causing serious disease in the affected limb; and perhaps killing the patient. Fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	 And this I have found through experiment and the long service and study that I have put into the art, based on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of my speech, because it pleases me not to take away from you the secret which is answered in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstration. Receive it now into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauterizations should be done, and chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And I say that cautery is suitable in all seasons, because the harm that occurs is put below by the help of cautery; and also if the cautery is necessary for pain that cannot wait for the time when greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 And do not think so, dear son, as the foolish doctors do; for the disease that is healed by cautery has no return; and they say so; but it is not so as they believe, because a cautery is nothing but a medicine that changes the complexion, dries the humors which cause pain, and works faster than any other medicine due to its effectiveness and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	 And it happens that the illness comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its power; and the superfluities are gathered in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless there are cauteries administered in the place where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as dental cauteries for pain, and similar things; and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worthwhile after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of healing in some illnesses and they are not effective, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cauterization is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 The ancients said that cauterization with gold instruments is more dangerous than with iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; but they were not telling the truth, for I have tested it and found that it is true in some men; and cautery with gold is indeed more dangerous than with iron, as they claimed.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 Nevertheless, when you heat a gold instrument, you cannot know when it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and if it cools too quickly; if it is heated too much, it melts in the fire; thus there are many obstacles to this.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 And therefore we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet, so that it may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	 of olive oil
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is useful against moisture and cold on the head, and there are two reasons for it: due to an illness called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and the ears, and due to excessive dreams and toothache and sore throat, and also all illnesses that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a laxative medicine, cleansing the head three or four times, according to what the patient's strength and constitution can bear; then make the patient's head bald.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on your thighs; after that, put the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes; where your middle fingers meet, there will be a bleeding; afterwards, heat the cautery called "olivare" for this purpose.
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it on the marked area, and in descending and holding your hand tight, turn it little by little; then lift your hand suddenly, and check the spot if you see a small bone; and if you do not see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards, take a piece of silk, and put in some soft cotton inside, and place on the spot, and let it stay for three days; after that, put on a damp cloth with butter; and leave it on until the burn is gone; then treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	 And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and therefore it helps to move (the limb).
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some of them said that one should let the cautery burn for so long that part of the bone is burnt, and then scrape off what has been burnt from the bone, and it should be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 And others say that one should let the cautery burn so long and push it so hard that a piece of bone comes off as wide as an arrowhead, which women use in their spindles, so that the humors are moved out; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one must cure and suture it. 》
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And these two ways of doing cautery do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a cause for fear; and I think that I must leave it; because the head (of the limb) is weakened by continuous natural discharges, as we testify in other members; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healing and beneficial to me, I use this method of working together for salvation. 》
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 When pain in the head becomes chronic and lasts long, then the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, and oils and poultices; and if one performs the cautery that we have mentioned before, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Take care if the head of the patient is of a strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize under that cautery a little bit which we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 Afterwards, make a cautery on each horn of the head until the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place which is called "vasselz"; and it is the place where one puts cupping glasses; and lift your hand so that you do not see until the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries of the horns must be thinner than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form.
dou cautere dou chief	 Of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 When sudden pain comes to one part of the head and the disease spreads to the eye, and the eye is purged by purgative medicines, and other cures have been performed as I mentioned in the division of diseases, and none of this helps: then make cauteries according to two methods, that is to say, with sharp medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 The cautery with sharp medicine is done by taking a clove of garlic and removing the skin, then placing it under both eyes, and then making an incision on the temple where the pain is in such a way that you can place the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it is placed, tie and bind it well and leave it thus for XII hours; and then untie it and draw out the clove of garlic, and let the wound remain thus II days or III; then apply a plaster soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 After the cure of inflammation until it is healed; and if you wish to do so, use some of the combustible medicines that I have written about in the doctrines of combustible medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery like this which is its form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 And it is called "clos" because its head is shaped like a bell or has a hollow in which there is a little opening in the middle; and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand steady while you turn it slightly until half the thickness of the iron is burned; and lift your hand so that the iron does not burn you, which is outside, and abundant blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 After, put cotton in vinegar water and place it on the spot for three days; then put moistened cotton in butter, and then treat the spot with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cultellare," do so entirely at the tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not very old.
de emigraine	 of a migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 When you treat a migraine as we have said before in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the previously mentioned cautery of medicine and iron is of no use to it, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery that is called "cultellare" until it is white; and so press it on the painful spot for half a line in length, and remove your hand once, and hold it so that you do not cut the artery and that you do not reach the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when one eats, and let the nerve have no regard except that it may move and that spasms do not come to the patient, and beware of the flow of blood from the artery when it is cut, for cutting has great fear and also for him who does not know it, and who is not a student and experienced; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how one stops blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it is necessary.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is tolerant, cauterize him in the head as we have said, and care for the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, along with a cautery that has two knives; and this cautery is better and more helpful than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When there is pain in the ear from cold, and one has worked with dissolving medicines and other cures that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery which is called "point", of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After puncturing all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move it a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place for piercing; let there be ten punctures around each ear; then heal the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 of the mouth's torment
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 Torment that must be cured by cautery is only that which arises from phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make cautery for similar conditions that come from dryness and nerve spasm.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 When you treat this type of torment that comes from phlegm, idres, and purging of the head and gargling, and it does not help, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little outside the temple, and the third between the two lips; and place the cautery in the healthy part, and make a cautery on the top of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery until half the head is burned; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And it is similar to the cupping we have mentioned earlier, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knife be a little larger; after the treatment of the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and there is no improvement and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, one in the place called «vasselz» as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and it should be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	 Of lead poisoning
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 At this illness, you must give the patient large pears and pills that cleanse the brain; afterwards, rinse the patient's head thoroughly, and place on their occiput a plaster of mustard as written in the treatise on plasters; and this is how to cauterize: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 If he is thus cured, it is good; and if not, perform three cauteries in the middle of the head descending to the neck, with two fingerbreadths between each cautery; and treat him as the others, and if you see fit, and the patient can endure it, make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two temples, and treat until he is cured; and let the cautery be called "olivare," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	 of coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and from what we have said before; after rising the head of the patient, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is tolerant, and the disease is strong, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until the largest part of the heart is burned, and lift your hand; then cure it until it is healed, and let the cautery that is called «olivare» that we have said before be.
de l’epilempsie	 of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptic should not use fire cautery except for the phlegmatic, and first must be moderated the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and able to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if it is an infant who cannot bear it, give him gargle and chew to moderate the brain often with good foods; afterwards rinse his head in the middle, and make a cautery there as we have said before, and a cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and able, make cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-sized as I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When because of melancholy there are superfluous humors or corrupted moisture and thick phlegm, then perform the cautery with these cauteries as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if because of melancholy the superfluity tends towards black bile, and the patient's body is moist, then give him to drink something that will cleanse his brain, as described earlier in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After shaving the patient's head, make a tourniquet of well-made linen, like a circle, and place it on his head; and let the patient sit cross-legged and be held firmly from all sides; then present the ointment, which is mixed with old sheep butter; and heat the bandage gently in the fire, so that the two (bandages) can be inserted; then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this for each patient once a week with other good treatment, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 If you see that you are cauterizing the wound by making several punctures throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This method of cautery moistens the brain equally; and then place a piece of cotton soaked in butter and goose fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	 from the edge of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When the edge first comes to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to purify the head, and guard it from all moisture, and make him sweat in the bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 After that, command him to shave his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the edge is on both eyes together, or one if the descent is on one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skull, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against an excessive flow of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then staunch it with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des artères et à l’incision la caution, comment tu l’étancheras; et parfois on fait un cautère ou une hâte sous les deux os derrière.
dou cors des larmes	 du corps des larmes
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 Lorsque les larmes des yeux sont anciennes et habituelles et sont sur les veines, ou près des artères qui apparaissent sur le front; et on voit que c'est une superfluité froide flegmatique, alors il fait le cautère que j'ai mentionné au début de l’œuvre descendante dans les yeux : un cautère au milieu du front, deux cautères sur les deux tempes, et deux cautères sous les deux os; et s'il y a plus besoin, alors on le cautérise sagement sur la racine des cheveux avec de petits cautères.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 from the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 When you medicate it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three nights of cooked food to drink; afterwards, anoint the head and make a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped scar; and make two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" on the two temples, one slightly below the eyebrows; and be careful not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the membrane of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery that is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	 For this reason, here is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if you see thus do two cauterizations on the two sources as long as the roots are; and do not leave your hand until one-third of the skin is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	 from the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are turned towards the inner corner and prick the eye, and then one does cauterization in two ways: namely with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When they are born and equal, then place the patient in your care; afterwards, draw on the skin of the eyes a figure that resembles the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then place moistened cotton with egg white and powdered perilla on the eye, then heat the cautery as described here.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards, cauterize on the figure that you have drawn bit by bit many times, until the skin is burned in that spot; and the sign of the healthiness of the work is that you see the skin retracted, and the hairs lifted to the height of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for III days, then place moistened cotton with butter until the scab is removed; after that, treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if after that the hairs come back, and the flesh is softened, then recommence the cautery on that same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the flesh is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The cautery of burning medication is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even. Then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and live alum, each one .З., and grind them together well. And do it hastily, so that it does not cool; then spread on the form that you have made like the myrtle leaf, and put on the flesh of the eyes; and if the disease is in only one eye, one should work in one, and if in both, likewise; and put wet cotton under the eye with egg white. And let the patient's head be in your healthy place and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press a little and the egg white all the times that the patient feels the burning of the medicine, for he feels the burning as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the bite has passed, lift up the skin, and look to see if the papillae have been raised in the same way as they would be by the constriction of fire or by an incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If not, then apply more medicine to the place where the medicine has not worked until your work is equal and your eyes are focused; then put on a piece of cotton soaked in butter until the burnt skin falls off, afterwards treat the place with an ointment called "dyafenis" and other things until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 Et si c'est nécessaire pour toi de faire très attention à ton travail afin que la médecine ne tombe pas dans les yeux.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then start the medicine again on that place which is made soft by the paper properly, as you did before; cure it until it heals; and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this let be your constraints; and do not be answered the right way for him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 Of the cure of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you cure fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cures do not benefit, then it is necessary that you perform cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Instruct the patient to place his head in your hand; and have the assistant place his head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, nor remove his head; then place wet cotton on top of egg yolk or juice of pepper on the eye; after heating the cautery which is thus: and it should be shaped like the feather of a vulture at the top where the cautery is; if you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, let it be like a tent; but nevertheless, this one that is shaped is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 After pressing the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, then open it, and draw forth the head; afterwards place a very hot cautery on top, and hold your hand at the cautery to the part of the neck above the eye, so that your hand does not make a mistake; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If not, then recommence the cautery again one or more times as needed, and leave it for three days; afterwards place a cotton swab moistened in butter, and use the cure of the desiccating ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply corrosive medicine so that the bone may be exposed; and do this according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a method of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Here is how to treat a fistula: first open the area; then place in the opening a thin camahan, whose shape is described below:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 and make it the size of a .З. of lead; and hold the camahan firmly in your hand, and let the patient not move at all, until the melted lead flows to his eye; and one should place on the patient's eye cotton moistened with egg white or vinegar: the lead thus cleanses the area of the fistula, and heals the healthy by marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then it is necessary to administer an opening at the nose, and bring the fistula back to the body of the nose according to its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	 fissures in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Very often, fissures occur on the lips that are called "hairs," and also on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these fissures as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not benefit, then heat a small blade-like cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it quickly in those fissures until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 When an abscess occurs in the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes putrefaction and a hole forms, and it becomes swollen and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not help: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards open or pierce the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron reaches the bottom of it, and in the rear place; and do this once or twice, after the treatment as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated thus, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 of tooth movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but to no avail, then place the head of the patient in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery as described later in such a way that you put a reed on the tooth; and put inside the hot cautery quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and start the cautery again according to your will; afterwards let the patient rinse his mouth with salt water, and let him keep it for an hour and spit out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this way the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the softened gum is restricted, and the moisture that caused decay is dried.
de la dolor des dens	 Of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 When tooth pain comes from cold, either from cold or air, and medicinal treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to use two types of cautery: cautery with butter and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 Cautery with butter is done by taking cow’s butter and placing it on the tip of an iron or brass spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a probe, dipping it in boiled butter, and place it quickly on the aching tooth until it cools down. Do this frequently until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. If you see that you have moistened wool and cotton in cold butter, place it on the aching tooth, and then apply hot iron until the fire reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The cautery with fire is such that you take a hollow iron or bronze tube, and it should be large enough that the smoke does not reach the patient's mouth; afterwards, heat the cautery, from which the form will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be relieved that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter when applying this cautery, and then rinse well; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And make a cautery on whatever part you wish, according to what you are able; and this is the form of the tube:
des scrophules	 of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When scrofula are from cold phlegm and moisture, and do not respond to digestion with medicines, then heat the cautery head as described below, and let it have two openings for the smoke to escape; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it there for three days; then place a cloth moistened with butter over it until the burn is gone; afterwards, treat the area with onions and lint until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 When moisture overcomes the passages of the nostrils, especially when this comes from a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the patient be first voided by soluble medicines; after which you make a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to come as far as the throat, but only a little from the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then make another cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and let the cautery be called "clavicle" as we have the form before; and treat the place as we said before until it is healed.
de la toust	 by coughing
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 When all and the illness of the nostrils are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is chronic, then make two cauteries on the breast in close places; and another cautery between the two breasts; and let the cautery be called "clavicle" according to the form that was said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if you see, make a cautery by pricking the entire cautery that is called "point" for which the form is thus in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or around them.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After treating the place according to what was said before, and let the cautery be at three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 And because the cauteries are lighter, therefore you make them in three doses.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 Afterwards, have the patient lie on his back and on his side; afterwards, lift the heart which is inside the tickling towards the two fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat up the cautery which has two nerves where it is located.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 And cauterize the heart until it perforates to the side, and there will come the figure of the cautery along with four other cauteries; and because of this, the cautery is made with the three-nerve cautery, which makes the figures of cauterization six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and that is the form of the three-nerve cautery:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is applied on this one nerve, which makes eight cauteries in total.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 After applying the cautery, bruise it with salt; then make the patient rest, and let the limb remain immobile for a long time until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it becomes dislocated again, which happens little, then make a cautery on the thick part of the dislocation, or many times in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When cold and much moisture come to the stomach so that it strains its complexion, and catarrh multiplies for him, and in the accustomed manner of treatment he does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and extend his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 From then on, he makes three cauteries. One under the scapula of the foot for the quantity of a finger, throughout the entire cautery, and two cauteries on the two sides so that the shape of the cauteries is in three corners, and there is such space between them that they are not joined together when they emit pus; and let the cauteries be so deep that they reach both parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this figure without alteration.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you want to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this figure, and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and signing on the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you wish; then cauterize throughout the cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the treatment of the previous treatment, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 When pain in the liver comes from cold and moisture and large flatulence, so that it is greatly removed from its natural complexion by superfluities; and if the patient is treated for what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him at all, then the patient must be placed on his back; and make three cauterizations according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, beyond the hypochondria, where the rib of a man comes; and let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger; and let the cauteries be long along the body, and do not press your hand too much at all the cautery; and let only half the hair be burned, and let the patient be upright on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, and stretch out his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if your will is to cauterize these cauteries with a knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, take care not to burn the entire heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and do not let it go as far as boiling, for the heart is very delicate in that place, and know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, the patient feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And then when this cure should be performed by the physicians, it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back; and then designate the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a grape, here is its form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And let him be cauterized with the cautery until the heart is burned, and it reaches up to the spleen, so that all the veins are completely emptied; after the cure according to the cure of the eyes until he is healthy; and it is not necessary for this cautery to be used by anyone other than one who has studied long in the art of medicine, and through whom fewer of these diseases have corrupted many times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Therefore he can boldly work, yet it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 of the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 The ancients said that one should make pleurisy cauteries with the root of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, as large as you can find, dry, and as thick and long as your fingers; moisten it in oil, take it to the fire, and cauterize I cautery between the ribs and the neck, and II small cauteries a little below in the part that is under the beard; and II cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, sloping back a little; and I cautery in the middle of the chest, and I another on the stomach, and I between the two shoulders, and II on the sides of the chest opposite the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make openly as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some ancient ones say that a man uses a fire cautery similar to a razor, and heats it and places it between the ribs, until it reaches that abscess; and thus it is for pain, as we have said in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula may form which cannot be healed.
de la mice	 of the pus
