Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	 When you treat the disease of the pus, as we have said in the division of treatments, and it does not benefit, then there are three kinds of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 One of the ways is that you make three or four cauteries, lining according to the length of the pus, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cautery, and let the patient lie on his back; and another way of cauterizing is that you heat the cautery which has two points, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the skin that is around the pus, where the ribs of the patient come towards the left, and the lifting should be according to the size of the head, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 Après i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part,
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 Après le cure, quant il a geté purriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut miex que li autre des cures devant dites.
de ydropisie	 de ydropisie
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 This means that cautery is not suitable for those with dropsy, except in the manner called "ascites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When you treat according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the navel, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the bladder, two behind the back on the spine, and one at the breast; and let the cautery be close to the edge of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	 Afterwards, leave the cautery open to discharge pus for a long time, and do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	 The shape of the cautery for the belly should be like a nail as we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	 Of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen for someone who is hydrocephalic and are full of yellow bile, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not enter too deeply, so that you can draw out the yellow bile, and let the cautery be of this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	 Afterwards, make two cauteries on each leg at the tip of the little toe; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries uncovered for a long time without curing, so that the bile can come out; afterwards, cure it as we have said for the other cures.
de la menoison	 of the arm
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	 When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by methods of treatment; and you see the patient well tolerating and of strong virtue, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before in the chapter on stomach cautery; and four subtle cauteries around the navel, each one with a small nail, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	 And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient tolerating it well, then make a cautery on the elbow, and one cautery on each hip, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	 About the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When the hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and they are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and they are treated as we have said by division, but it does not help, then make cauteries: III on the spine of the back, those which are all outside under the navel, a little at a time in triangulating, and I cautery below the buttocks II; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the food does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then give him I large cautery on the stomach as was said before, and I other on the liver, and I other on the bladder with all the cautery covered; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After caring for the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	 of the condition known as "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	 When you treat althelul, heat the cautery that looks like a razor, and then place it completely ablaze on the treated althelul; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein where the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of althelul, then cauterize each one as we have said; after the treatment with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchatim, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	 of a poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	 When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, which we will describe in its place, then such a disease occurs that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 When someone has a fistula and it is swollen and gives off putrid and corrupt moisture, you should probe it with a very fine needle, and make sure you know the depth of the needle throughout its entire length.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 Then heat the cautery that looks like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the depth at which the needle has entered, and repeat the cauterization until the putrid and corrupt flesh is burned, once or twice or three times, as needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are in it, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and intestines, beware of these places, and do not perform this procedure except in a fleshy place, and consider that it is not persistent; afterwards, treat the place until it is healed, and if the place is healed and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; but if the matter is not removed, know that the place is pierced, and the bone is corrupted at its root; and so as one of those which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	 Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	 When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and of great flatulence, and does not act like that of a woman, then it is necessary for you to make a cautery on the kidneys on one side and on the other with a clavicle cautery as we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and they will bring greater help.
de la vessie	 of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	 When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then make a cautery on the lower part of the abdomen above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right side and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as your thumb; and you may also make a cautery on the back if needed; and let the cauteries be flat according to the shape mentioned before.
de la marris	 For the piles (hemorrhoids)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	 When the hemorrhoids are cold and moist, preventing conception, and the menstrual flow is corrupted and delayed in its course; and when it does come, there is great pain: then one should make three cauteries around the anus, as we have said for the cautery of the bladder, and two on the back; and let the cauteries be flat, as we have said.
de la hainche	 of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	 When the viscous moisture descends to the hip joint, and because of this it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the place of separation is found to be visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip joint with a circular cautery, and mark before the place around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is inside the circle; and let the cautery be such that it was used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if this cautery is not available to you, then make three large olive-sized cauteries, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the joints; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	 Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	 When pain comes in the joint of the hip, and it is from cold or moisture, and the patient is cured with what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the illness is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 After that, perform cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 Fire cautery is according to many methods, one of which is such that you cauterize on the joint of the hip three triangular cauteries in this form, and make each of them deep and large, and there should be between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cautery be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, so that there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if you see, then cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the hip; but do so in such a way that the circle contains all the hip, and all the thickness of the heart is burnt.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the manner in which one proceeds with sciatica, when the pain is confined to the hip and does not extend down to the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if it extends to the thigh and leg, then make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is located, and one cautery four fingers above the ankle, slightly towards the left; and let the cautery be cutaneous, and let the thickness of the heart be burnt; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the two toes or close thereto, then cauterize where he feels the pain three or four times with the cautery which is called "point".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	 And if necessary, do more; and if he knows that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a lancet or circular cautery, and be sure in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause more harm and constriction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it so long that the leg became completely swollen, as well as the foot, and all the foot was eaten away and rotted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a bellyache from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two places together, make a cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the wise say in the cautery of the hip, for which there is this manner: make such an iron tool and let it be at the tip as thick as a nail of a digit, or a little less, and let it have prongs and let the prongs be from one to the other of space the quantity of a nut of a pouch; and let the prongs be covered on two parts, and let them also be like needles, and there should be a well-made iron handle; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let it be heated until it is all red and casts sparks, and then place it on the boil of the sick hip, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with a cautery again, and leave it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the care of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	 Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its gaze, and if we see few who use it; however, this is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured, and there where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The cautery of burning medicine is such that you make an instrument with interwoven strands where the margin of the door descends. It should be made of brass or iron, with one long side and two holes on top, each the size of a finger's width. They should be open at both ends and join together in this manner:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 Afterwards, place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his healthy side, and then place your hand very high up on the box of the hip; afterwards, throw between the two circles of the awl a little hot coal that has been heated in the fire, and leave it there for an hour. Let the patient endure the heat and the burn of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because it experiences burning as if by fire; and when the burning has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hip with gentle heat, and leave it thus for three days, and apply butter until the blackness of the scalding is removed; and leave it for three more days so that the putrefaction can be drawn out; and this would be the last aid after the treatment of onions until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, then make an instrument that holds heat according to what you have done for the hip in the same way; and this is the manner of hot heat, and I have written about it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take quicklime and slaked lime, equal amounts of each, grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 where there is a small hole outside so that the point of a razor can enter; and put on top of this pot another well-sealed pot, and place quicklime and lime powder on top until there are two fingers’ width above the powders before you have it well sealed with your hand; and leave it like this until the water descends and collects in the bottom pot, then take all that water and throw it back onto the quicklime and lime powder as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then it will be very acidic and is used in many works of medicine and for other cauteries on members because it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize the hip well, such as terebinth, anacardium honey, and lime mixed with soap.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 Et (And)
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says in this manner that you should take fresh and dry litharge, grind it very finely with a little fat, and apply it to the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and let it sit; and leave it for three hours, by which time the patient should no longer feel the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then have him enter the bath so that his body is slightly warmed, and put him to bed, and all the pain will go away and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use such a cautery with these medications unless it is after the evacuation of pus.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with wool of sheep, it helps very much; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the big toe of the foot and the one called phalanx.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Then take dry goat dung and press it into coal until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the wool, and let it remain until it is stained; and do this again, and do not stop doing so until you sense by touch that it reaches the hip, and the pain ceases; and this type of cautery is called "goat cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	 Of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	 When pain comes to the back, from falling or striking or from excessive evacuation, or from similar cold spread material, none of these resemble cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	 Il is necessary after the patient has been voided of pungent pills or other similar substances that one make on his back, where the pain is located, three lines marked with ink, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the strength and amount that the patient can tolerate; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see fit, make III cauteries or IV at the middle of the cautery clavile according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	 Often this disease comes to small children, and the sign of its beginning is that they have narrow veins when they rise, and fear; and you find in the lower spine of the back and with us the appearance which comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	 When you see this and wish to cure it, then cauterize it with the cautery of that according to this manner.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 So that the cautery penetrates each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, then cauterize around the spine with a penetrating cautery two or three lines deep, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After curing the place until it is healed as we have said, and beware that you do not administer a cautery in the region of the spine of the nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	 of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	 When the pain of the joints comes from moisture that is spread to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which doctors call "podagra" properly, and when it is due to a cold cause and drugs cannot cure it, then it should be cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary that you prick on the sole of the foot, make a cautery over all the area called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pains reach up to the knees and other joints, which happens often, make cauteries on each knee III or IV from each side, all olive cauteries; and if you need more, do more, but keep your hand no longer than it takes for the cautery tip to be burnt.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the hands, make a hole around the wrist II lines; and if there is any pain in the two (fingers), then make holes on each joint and on the palm of the hand; and if the pains reach up to the ribs or up to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and give him medicine. ię And if there are pains in the feet, make a hole around the ankle II lines; and if there is any pain in the toes, then make holes on each joint and on the sole of the foot; and if the pains reach up to the knees or higher, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and give him medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you give him good care and purge phlegm, he will be cured with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	 of the dislocation of the hip
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When dislocation occurs in the hip and the buttocks descend to the thighs, which is new, you should ensure that when you have it treated, he does not move that day; and let him use things that open the belly so that the feces leave his belly; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his leg until the buttocks are restored, and bring them back to your hands, and place a sign under the dislocation on the bone of the elbow, and let it be like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 As long as he is white and casts shadows.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Until they return to their place; and the assistant holds his hand so that they do not return backwards; and work well the thighs on the patient, and put under him one pillow and one sergeant on the thighs, and another on the foot which holds the hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it right and straight until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again until you reach the bone; and subtly watch that the testicles do not protrude when you make the cautery; so that you do not burn them; and so that the patient does not die or other evils.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And it is necessary that the cautery for children be fine according to their size, and also large for adults according to their size; after three days, cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is gone; then cure with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his nourishment be prolonged, so that the boils do not come out when he tries to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wants to get up, let him have a well-made belt and wear it for another forty days; and let him rest well, not exerting himself too much, and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and of laughing too hard; and when he follows this advice, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	 of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When ruptures occur in other bellies and are noticeable, and you see that they no longer grow, perform the cautery of cautery again according to its size, and burn one-third of the heart; then treat it as we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery like this:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first sign the place where it begins and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another below, and then hold your hand in the middle of the whole cautery firmly.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	 Of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes in some limb, whether from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and medical treatment is not effective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins," and the cautery should be made according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of the twisting and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, perform another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom that it should move to the nearest limb, which is why you must perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	 of healing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The illnesses are helped sometimes by cautery with great benefit, and especially the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 When you see it being cauterized, take care if the illness is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and neither subsides nor lingers, and you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head at the nape, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two temples, and one behind on the occipital bone; and let your hand be such that the cautery reaches the bone, and so that the scales come out so that the vapors of the gross humors may escape; and cauterize on the bladder as before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	 And if the contamination is spread everywhere; and it is clearly lost, then you must cauterize with these cauteries that we have mentioned earlier, and one cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another nearby, and two on each shoulder; and two on each rib, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the back of the knee, lest you burn them; and sometimes a man makes a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more I do of cautery, the more aid I give him, and it benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel pain from cautery as the healthy person feels it, because his body is already completely corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And the cauteries must be large and small according to the members and the joints, as you will find in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After curing, apply a mixture of crushed chickpeas with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When inflammation occurs in any member and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it does not heal, then I make cauteries on the member according to its size; and let the cautery be a little deep into the thickness of the skin; then cure it with onions until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes one cauterizes at the hand and at the foot and at the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb; and thus the swelling is removed; nevertheless, no one should interfere with it unless he is knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves.
de albaras	 of apples
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed and medical remedies are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery, not too deeply, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes; then treat it with a mixture of chickpea flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from the colon and almond tree, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and let it air in that place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	 The treatment of cancer by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When cancer first appears and you see it stop, then cauterize around the entire circumference of the cancer with a cautery that looks like a circle.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 Nevertheless, the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the cancer; but this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen sometimes; and a more reasonable thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circular," as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	 of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it is slow to heal, either because of the patient's superfluity or due to old age when they are decrepit (that is, too old) and have little blood, or because of time; and you see that it is hastening to heal: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 Because she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you see her through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery with what is in this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it on the surface in such a way that the course of the corruption is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the cure, so that he may be perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	 The cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another manner of disease there is which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a gnawing away at the members, for it gnaws at the members just as fire does dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this disease in a place that can bear fire together with the iron, then heat the cauterizing irons very small and large according to what is needed for the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize it from all sides until you remove all the corruption and nothing remains of it, so that all that is corrupted may be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and place on the cauterized places a plaster with oil until the burns of the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the treatment of flesh-producing wounds.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if after three days you see that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then begin the cautery again on what remains of the corrupt place.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this mistake has sometimes been cured with cold medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure with cold medicine in the previous section: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	 of leeks that grow at the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 It often happens that on the soles of the feet a disease grows which is called "clots" in our opinion, and it is a large wart-like thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cautery for this disease is according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Fire cautery is that you heat a cautery like a goose quill, and it should be made of good iron so that it can penetrate the clot on all sides, and there should be subtle edges; after that, place it very hot onto the clot, and turn your hand completely around the clot until it reaches the base of the clot; and leave it this way for three days until it begins to produce pus; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the clot will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the area of the burn with aloe vera until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if they are turned outward toward the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should bring hot water cautery to it; and it is done in this manner: take a rod of brass or iron, or a goose quill, and place it on the wart and the altar (i.e., the wart), that is to say, the common wart; and place the rod so that it covers all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the rod comes to the root of the wart, and let the hot water find its way deep down to the root; and allow the patient to endure the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave him thus, and it will be completely uprooted from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Then do one after another, until you have extracted all that are in the body, then treat the wounds that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	 The treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	 When someone trembles from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever, or other causes, it is necessary that you make four cauteries, or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; then the trembling will stop, and the health will hasten from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	 Of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes there appear on the surface of the body baths or stinking pustules that come from large corrupt substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 If it is necessary at first when the boils appear, then make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, whose tip should be seized in the fire, or a long root of aristolochia, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the superfluidities from which they come are broken, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	 when the vein is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	 Many times there is a great outpouring of blood from the vein that is cut at the wound that appears in front, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a very serious matter to faint.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	 And nevertheless when this happens to someone, hasten to place your finger on the vein wound, and hold it very firmly until the blood is quiet under your finger, and no drop comes out; then put in the fire several small and large olive cauters until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and the place where the vein is open, and place the cauter on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cauter there until the blood is coagulated.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	 And if it spurts out when you remove your finger from the vein and the cauter is extinguished, then quickly take another one from the cauters that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	 And do not stop doing this one after the other until the blood is stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stopped, especially when the artery is large, except by one of the four methods we have mentioned: by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and held appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	 Whoever administers the stopping by tightly binding with cloth or placing burning things on it, or other similar things, if it does not help, then it is of no use.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	 And if this happens to anyone and he does not have a doctor or present medicine, then he should place his finger directly on the vein wound as we have said, and press it firmly until it is constricted over the wound and over the vein; and do not move the finger, but apply cold water often, so that it is very cold, until the blood is frozen and swollen and constricted; and make arrangements in advance for those things he will need for cauterization and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	 Here begins the second book of the treatment of hernias
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	 We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases for which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and the preparations and causes and tools and types of cauterization; and I placed that chapter from the head down to the feet, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same method so that what one seeks may be found more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	 Et avant que je commence ceci, il est nécessaire, cher fils, que vous sachiez qu'il y a plus de danger et de peur dans ce chapitre que dans le premier des cautères, et pour cette raison, il faut prendre plus de précautions.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	 Car dans le travail de ce chapitre, il arrive souvent une évacuation de sang lors de l'ouverture d'une veine, et lors de l'incision sur un abcès, et dans les soins des plaies, et dans l'extraction des flèches, et dans la coupe de la pierre, ainsi que des choses semblables; où il y a du doute et de la peur, et beaucoup en meurent.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 Et je vous avertis de ne pas entreprendre de folie.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For very many types of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 if they come of such who are so afflicted with their illness that they die easily from the madness caused by their illness and the severity of their condition; and of these one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And there are some who give you their wits and say: "wait, I am healed"; and the illness is insolent.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more consideration in your honor than in your greed, and do not open your doors foolishly but wisely to those whom you are certain of, and from whom you can take credit and praise; and use prognosis and diagnosis in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, glory, and a lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	 Very dear son, Our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe from the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	 Now I have arranged this chapter for you by discussing in chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cautery, which I have discussed from head to foot, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	 full of water from the head
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	 Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the delivery is too tight around the child's head; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	 And I have never seen this illness except in children, and all those that I saw were approaching death; and therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave the work of such cures.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	 And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head swelled every day so much that it could not support it; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone on the forehead, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, you should cut into the head a wide slit; and it should be as long as II of us, so that the moisture runs out; and see here the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	 If the moisture is thicker, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, as shown in this figure:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	 And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the cracks of the head open on each side, and the water jumps strongly when you press it with your hand inside, and this is not answered: then you must split the head into three splits in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, extract all the moisture outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 After closing the splits with bandages and powders, put wine and oil on them, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then release it, and heal the wound by degrees and dressings, and let the head be held evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	 And another way of incision is that you look at where the greatness of the abscess opens, and the gathering of water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	 Cut there where the abscess opens, and the gathering of water, and make an opening according to your ability; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and let blood flow out, so that the patient may die from bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	 of pus
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	 When it happens to someone that they have a disease called 'catarrh' in the eyes or in the bladder, and the disease is chronic, and medical treatment does not help, then the final cure is fire cautery with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 It is therefore necessary that when you see them swell up, the patient should bend his neck back; then rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient stretch his neck with all his might; then observe where the vein beats, and the places of one and the other are behind the ears, and they are few in number; then mark the places from below, then cut each with a sharp spatula of two parts, as deep as the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done across the width of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	 And if you see it, push the spatula under the artery and cut above, slicing as you would two dices across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	 And when the vein is cut, the blood jumps up continuously outward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery does not open to the touch, then you must measure the length of three fingers, and sign the spot with ink and cut down to the bone; and as for how much blood should come out, it is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can bear and the filling of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains a point of pus on the bone, then cut it away so that such pustules do not form, then press the wound and bind it, and continue the treatment with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	 of a migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	 When an old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and ancient foolishness and similar things, and he is treated by various methods of medication and none of it helps him at all, we will extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 And the manner of extracting them is such that the patient shaves the hair from his temples and feels for the artery that appears in the temple, because it appears well through its pulsation, and there are few people who do not have it; and if it is not found, then let the patient tighten his neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and moisten the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula of which here is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then skin the hide lightly until you reach the artery, then draw it up to the pincers, and separate it well from the cloths that are beneath each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it with the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 Because if it is not cut, the blood will not flow at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	 And draw out the blood from the VI part until the III part; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you bind it in two places with a strong double silk thread to prevent infection before the wound is closed, and the bleeding should come gradually; then cut off the excess between the two ligatures at that very moment, and then, if you wish, cauterize with a hot iron until the bone, so that the fingers are completely cut off; this is a bad outcome if the patient has a fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	 For the cautery is used to finish moisture; therefore, it is of greater help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	 And for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the place with old cotton and apply well-made compresses; and when you unbind them, cure with dry medicines that produce flesh, and with compresses, until he is healed; and if the blood flows from the artery as long as you work there, hasten with the copper cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and press it with your hand so that the blood may be stopped; and if you do not have this present, put your finger on the place until the blood is congealed, and sprinkle the place with cold water until the blood ceases, and hold it as it should be held; and what is easier and lighter in the extraction of arteries than that you cauterize the vein of this cutting cautery on both sides, but let the cuts be well spaced to retain their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	 When the instrument is too dull, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And there should be one finger width between the two knives, and then when you have joined the two places, place the burning iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let the two ends be far apart because this is not a complete burn from beginning to end; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	 tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	 When tears descend from the veins on top of the head, and medical treatment does not help, and you see the patient's face turn red, and they feel a pulsation in their forehead like shivering; and their eyes are dull and moist so that the eyelashes have fallen out, and the eyelids are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
