Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And the ancients called it "cure for contusion," and what you must do for the patient who has this illness is to let the hairs on his forehead grow long; then make three incisions in his forehead, equal in length according to the size of the forehead; and one of these incisions should be as if two fingers wide, going down the middle of the forehead until the nose, and the other two on each side above the eyebrows, and beware of cutting the arteries that are on each side above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be three fingers wide across; and prepare a piece of sponge and many cloths to wipe away the blood, then apply the sharp spatula in two parts as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 From the incision that is towards the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the heart that is between the two cuts on all the tissue that is above the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second, and then strongly extract this instrument.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	 insert into the first cut the instrument called "cultellary," which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other; this is its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And place the cutting side towards the soft flesh of the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it opens the heart; and then make another cut in the middle cut to the other outside; and then draw out the blood equally, and press the place for the taken blood; then put in each cut a tent of old cotton, and put on wet cloths in wine and oil and honey, and be careful that any abscesses come there; and on the third day remove the bandage, and apply a large plantain poultice with cold water, then treat it with an ointment made from basil and rose oil, and other treatments for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	 About the head of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 When someone has an acute cataract, you see the eyes watery and small, and it weakens the sight, and the eyelids burn; and the hair falls out, and there is a headache, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that those substances and that cataract come from many veins, and the remedy for it is as follows.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And what you must do is instruct the patient to shave their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one on the temple.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 And begin the incision from the left temple to the right, and let the cut go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then scrape between the two lips of the cut and put old cotton and linen bandages in it; then bind over it wet cloths soaked in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when they are removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow on it, then cure with drying agents that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 En such a manner: take two parts of flour from wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and administer it in these wounds to heal flesh completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 of the stopping of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 All that falls into the ear is one of four things: grain, animal, stone from a mine or similar thing like iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing substance, such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When something falls into the ear that does not belong there, such as a stone or any other thing that is not suitable for the ear and cannot grow in the ear, put the ear in sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, drop some drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then perform extraction; and make him sneeze by condiments, and stop his nostrils when he sneezes, and wrap pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Much of the time this cure causes a fever; and if it does not cause a fever, let him be treated with subtle lancets, the form of which is here described.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 If it does not cause fever with lancets, it is good; if not, then apply an extraction with a fine needle of small thickness; and if it does not cause fever this way, make a tube of bronze and insert the end of the tube into the ear canal strongly, and stop up that which is around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then draw out strongly, for much of the time it causes fever as we have said; and if it does not cause fever in this manner, take glue of the sort from which birds make their nests, and put some into a suitable instrument, and place a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and draw out strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it does not jump out of all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before an abscess and spasm come there; and the manner of the cutting is such that you first make the patient drink cephalic wine, and draw blood according to the measure of its virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat or dependent place; and let the cut be like a moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 And if there is a grain inside and it swells, administer an extract; and if it cannot come out, then administer a subtle and thin ointment according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear; rather, make many pieces of it; then draw it out with subtle tweezers and a syringe, as we have said, so that the extraction may be easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Therefore, in water that falls into the ear, the patient should first use sneezing-inducing condiments and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let it lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 S’ele saute fors per ceus, ceo est boin.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 And if not, then take many small stones according to the length of your thumb, light and thin, and warm them slightly in the fire. The patient should put one into the opening of his ear, and jump on his feet from the other side, and strike with another stone onto the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out completely. And if you wish, take a reed, put one end into the ear, and hold the other end in the fire until the thickest part of the reed is burned; then repeat this with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 In the extraction of an insect, if it is small, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, use extraction by tweezers; and this is the lightest thing to remove that may be in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in dealing with distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sunlight; if any worms appear, then extract them with fine tweezers, and if none appear, then take a reed of which there is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And inject the most subtle part into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then draw out all the wax; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not come out, then plug the ear with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not come out strongly as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven for killing worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations; and thus distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And let it be of silver or copper with a small hole at the bottom and a lid on top for distilling; and to press the distillation inside, use a well-made copper tool for this purpose, and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the point; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you want into the ear, and let the ear be in the ear; then insert the scraper with all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the hollow of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little heated over the fire before it is distilled into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 of ear blockage
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 No child is born without any hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults by blockage of a wound, or bone born inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is only lack of the hole, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 That which comes deep and cannot be seen is of serious concern in many cases, and in that which can be seen, it is necessary to place the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see the hair apparent, then work all this spatula of which here is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 And let it be sharp and cutting edge both in front and behind all plainly, so that it does not wound the ear; if the lancing is of flesh or body of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the lancing goes deep into the ear, then take a fine, light rasor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the lancing which the patient feels pain at hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tampon according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Do this every day until the wound is healed, where you take a linen cloth and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swell, then you must remove the cloth and use another cloth soaked in ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are described in the section on distillations.
de la char des papieres	 of paper's flesh
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 This inflammation that comes in the eyes when they are wet and then dry, you should dilate them with tweezers and pincers, and scrape out the matter with a spatula made from its roots; then place powdered vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 Et si sans en decort, then you cauterize it with the subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision is worthwhile; and often they regrow, when some part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	 of gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Many times in the eye there are things that seem like gravel in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called «hail», and it is a large collection of moisture in the upper and lower eyelid; the work is thus: take care if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is easy to know; then make an incision widely, then peel each part lightly, then take with tweezers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it without puncturing the skin slightly, then it does no harm to the patient; and if the tear is large, then stitch it with a single suture, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, then do not use force, for the ointment restores it quickly and regenerates flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And if the boil descends into the ear towards the upper part, then puncture the skin, and extend the boil with pincers, and cover and press it from both sides; and if the skin is separated by the incision, it does no harm; and when the boil is covered, lift the skin with salt water, and treat the place with that which regenerates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	 of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is a fat that is produced in the tissue of the eyelids, and this occurs more often in children than in adults, and it greatly irritates their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the sunlight because tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they always lie on their backs, and sleep face up, and their eyelids below their eyebrows are moist with exinach that opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the place between your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 And the manner of working is that the patient places his head in your hand; and then take a cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach from each part, then place it on him; and press between your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit as wide as the incision for a vein; and cut the skin to the depth until you reach the exinach; and in many cases the exinach comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 Pull it out then all at once with a piece of cloth between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread; and be careful not to enter into the cleft, that you do not come all the way to the eye, that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the cleft, then widen the cleft slightly until it opens; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten clean cloths in vinegar and water, and place on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are such men who break reeds and put them on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Puis le cure, so long as he is cured.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if a hot abscess forms at the place, treat it with soothing poultices until he is cured.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 When hairs grow on the eyelids that are different from natural ones and they become inflamed, they harm the eyes and bring on various diseases such as tears, swelling of the eyelids and styes, which can lead to blindness; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by medicinal ointment as described in the previous chapter on cautery, or by incision and suturing, or by caustics, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid of the eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, then insert a needle with all its thread above; and let this be near the edge of the eyelid where the hairs are born near these hairs, and pull the thread over the entire eyelid, and turn it to the razor; then cut in the part below the eyelid, below the close hairs, covering all the way from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the eyelid, then make on the eyelid a figure of incense, as the myrtle leaf, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you wish to raise the eyelid which has been said.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And for those who need it, cut a large quantity of the paper according to how soft the paper is; then make all the spatula above the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large lacrimal up to the small one; and let one of the cracks be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then apply the ointment into one of the two angles of the heart, then peel it all off; then join the two lips with a stitch of a needle all along I thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the superfluous threads above the two eyebrows adhere to any gluey things, if you want to do this; and if not, then don’t worry about it, but leave the stitch and the threads for III days or IV; then treat the wound without a stitch with dry and constricting things, because the paper revives at the joining of the wound and its healing, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear; and there is another way: which is that you seal the paper with a shape that is like the leaves of myrtle, as we have explained, with III ointments uncovered according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 Then cut those who surmount the small forces equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and insert it into the figure; and insert another thread next to the large tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and gather the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin you have cut, as we have said, then join the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with wax and similar ointments that alleviate pain; and sometimes it happens that the hair on the skin turns: then you should use what we have said about the incision; but stitching in one way or another is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 The cure of the hairs is thus: you must turn the skin and the hole inside as I have said, then make two hairs by art, and two subtle ligaments as long as the skin and wide as the spatula; and cut the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one with the other subtly on what stands out from the eyelid skin, and strongly tighten the two hairs of the two parts; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is tightened will die and darken and rot, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it delays, then cut it with forceps, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the skin is lifted, the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the two hairs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 The work is such that you take a subtle needle and put in it a soft and subtle silk thread. Then assemble the heads [of the needles] and tie each of them subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the handle another brief and subtle silk thread, and tie the ends of the thread together; then let the patient place his head on your healthy side. And let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a subtle and small work; then push the needle all along the handle into the root of the hair next to it, and make it pierce the skin hastily until you pull it out above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to above the handle, and put in the handle that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out all along the handle with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the hair is removed and does not grow back with it, you will draw out the hair beneath all the way along the length of thread that you have placed there, until the hair comes out from above and you can see it with your eye; then you will remove the hair and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh heals; and if the hair is small, accompany it with a long natural hair from the eyelashes, and let them grow together until they are long enough, then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the pustule of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "aleacrati" or pustule comes to the eye, there are two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting or from cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the manner of the work in it is that you split open this scar, and separate its edges, and place inside tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not necessary that you use in its treatment things that dry out and constrain.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, then the disease returns worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and wash it with water or althea and linseed that are cooked, and ointments of diaquilon melted in some of the oils, and wrap it in a bandage, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 And the treasure of your care is such that you must ensure it does not heal according to the form it was before; and these works that we have said are not outside but in accordance with this illness, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness, which is truly called "axacrati", is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from a wound and a split and a burn and similar things; and the way of the work in it is such that you take a needle with two threads on it, and pierce the flesh from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread passes through two layers of the flesh; then press the flesh down over all the needle, and cut off one broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the slit, and turn the paper, and make two slits on each side inside the paper; and let the ends of the two slits be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and let one angle be made such that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are sharp below, from what follows the paper, then join the two severed parts, and sew them with a linen thread; then follow the cure as we have said for softening medicines and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 And if the disease comes from a split or stitch or cautery, then you must make a clean split under the hairs of the papers; and according to what is said above; then drain between the two livers of a tent, as I have said; and one should perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares an engine of all his power how he may bring back the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs for work and instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	 of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When this union happens to many people in such a way that the paper above is glued with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural works, then it is necessary that you push the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and hold it with tweezers, until you cut what is hard to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer that the too sharp spatula hurt the eye; and let your incision, from which you scrape that union, be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural shape; and all that union is healed, and sometimes in the eye there is salt water, and raise with fresh water, and with honey; then put between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool moistened with plenty of egg; and after three days use honey and things that are gluing until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 You should know that the nail is according to two kinds: one is nervous and similar to a hard syphacus, and another which is not nervous but is similar to frozen white moisture; if one touches it with iron and tries to pinch it with pincers, no one can do so. And both resemble each other at the beginning of the great eyelid, and grows little by little until it covers all the sight, and all the light, and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 And the manner of the incision is such that the patient places his head in your hand, then opens the eyes; and removes the paper from your hand, then rolls the nail with small pincers, and raises it up; then take a needle, and put one horsehair, or cow's hair, or ox hair into it, and one strong thread; and fold the point of the needle a little and insert it into the middle of the nail, and pierce all the way with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and raise it up, and scrape off all the skin that follows the root and the silk to the hair until the head, then cut off the remainder in the root of the eyelid with all the subtle spatula and small forces, and leave the natural flesh in the eyelid, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears habitually; and sometimes they tie the nails only at the onyx, and to the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft spatula from which this is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And take care that the mucus does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the prunelle is not pierced; and after the incision, throw into the eye a little bit of crushed salt, and made from litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with what is needed so that it may heal.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the hook cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is treated with medicine; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, work on the eye of the patient, and take a small amount of mucus according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 Et gently scrape the nail from above, and if you see that it is not thinning and the root approaches, then drip into the eye a collyrium made of lead and red and burnt lead powder, and plug the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If anything in the eye is opposed to this, such as an abscess, then let it be, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 And if the appearance of flesh from the tear duct enters the eye to great harm, then suspend it at the corner, and cut off a part but not all, so that the body of tears does not come there; then drip into the eye red collyrium which is made from lead.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 of the flesh that grows upon the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 of some men's eyes there grows sometimes red flesh, which covers the pupil and extends onto the eyelids and turns them outwards, and it appears like a rose on a column; and the procedure is such that the patient places his head in your lap, then you operate on the eyes, and remove all that flesh into suitable vessels for this purpose, and support with forceps; then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting to the razor's edge until the end, and be careful not to damage the eye during the operation; and let the incision of the spatula be as we said in the incision of the nail and small forces by which one removes the pustule, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with boiled linen thread on which you have dripped red vinegar or similar corrosive medicines, and place over the eye a thick cotton pad with egg white so that it is secure from hot abscess; and if anything remains and the pus surmounts the wound, and you doubt hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the hot abscess with soothing remedies; then return to your operation until it is healed, and thus do whenever flesh grows in the eye by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 And yet it is necessary that you choose the treatment for each weak eye according to nature's way; and for accidental ways, by ironwork; and do not place your hand in any of these works until you see that this member can bear the work.
des voines des eulz	 of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 If the veins of the eyes are red and cover the eye, they hinder sight and weaken the eye daily.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Therefore, first look to see if the eye in which there is redness is sound, and there is no other disease besides the redness; then treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then raise those veins with a very fine double needle according to your skill.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 Et soient two ointments by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 Then anoint subtly those subtle veins with those forces, and wipe away the blood hour by hour until you see those strong veins withdraw from the eye; and take care not to wound the eye with the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very eager in your work so that you only strike those veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red choler to corrupt what remains of the black.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	 And if you do not have the power to heal all of them in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye from things that ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and the abscess is hot, then begin again according to this manner which is before until they are healed; and these are the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	 Of the fistula of the anus
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 Physicians call this type of fistula «arissati»: when you treat it with cautery and burning medication as I have previously described, and it does not heal, there is an abscess within it that you should open above the abscess where it should burst open, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, use all the tools whose shapes are described here; it is called «sharp head», and it should be made of iron or steel, and it should be pointed like a file as shown in the following illustration:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And place it on the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the area with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the wound is healed and flesh grows back, and the body of the bow remains healed, and it stays this way for forty days without reopening or becoming infected, and no bad incident occurs, then know that it is cured; if not, there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: and it is that you discover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is discovered, then take a reed according to this form, and let the head be of iron with three angles, and let the shaft be tapered to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place it on the bone near the eyelid, and remove your hand from the eye by a thumb's width, then turn the entire reed until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the wind comes out if he holds his hand to his nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the wound hardens, the matter goes to the nose; this is a lighter procedure for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the eye is entirely open and there is no disturbance or narrowing of the pupil, you must bandage the patient; then heal it, then apply cupping glasses without pricking to draw out, then place on the eye a plaster made of acacia, aloe, frankincense, and myrrh, then bandage the eye, and cover with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is such that you take cloths soft enough, and fold each one four times, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye needs; then bind tightly with a hard bandage, and reapply the cupping glasses to draw out without pricking; then remove the cups and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the bandage softens, you must bind it very tightly; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye begin to heal, that is good; if not, then repeat the plaster and the cloths and the bandage and the cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 Of the breaking of a woolen garment
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 When disruption occurs in the woolen garment, it opens up and there comes out pieces of paper like a grain of resin, which is frightening to see; then if you see it closed, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the part below until it reaches above, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the armhole; and pierce it through, leaving the first needle according to its arrangement; then cut around the place of the double thread and tie a piece of the woolen garment around it, and secure it well, then draw out the needle and put on an ointment of moistened linen with plenty of egg; and leave it until the threads blend with the woolen garment, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restricted by the woolen garment all around in a circle until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the eye gives a great appearance, prick it with a subtle spatula that goes deep into the eye, and drain the whitish moisture from the eye, and put in immediately; then withdraw it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	 of the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease which is called «alcunnati» is nothing but the socket of the eye which resembles descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of appearing in work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the socket appear above your eyes; then it should be inserted, and not descend, and the light should be darkened, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not go down, know that it is water, and if the descent of the socket is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If the patient is seated between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make an incision on the horny tissue at the corner of the eyelid by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny tissue and the cornea, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, instill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	 of the eye's water
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have seen similar waters in the division, and those that need to be pierced; act accordingly to the health of the situation.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, out of direct sunlight; and bind the healthy eye very tightly; then place the eyelid in your left hand if the eye is the left one, or in your right hand if the eye is the right one; then take in your right hand, if the eye is the left one, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is the right one; then place the tip of the instrument next to the cornea at the thickness of a ray in that white part of the eye towards the minor lacrimal duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and turn your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty place; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda hole be at the depth of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone in that eyelid because of the clarity of the horny tissue, and afterwards place the instrument where the water is, then press it under a way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If the water descends now, let the patient see it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After resting it a little, and if the water rises again the second time, place the fire with the instrument, and when it is in and does not rise, gently draw Almagda by turning your hand little by little; and then put in a bit of soft gemstone, and remove his eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then place on the outside of the eye a wad or piece of wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg, and bind with healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, put it on with a poultice made from plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if Almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "Alberit," which looks like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And so puncture the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle; then put in almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a suitable bed, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be free from all movements, and let him take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and let him be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you do this beforehand, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If abscesses come, uncover the eye before the seventh day, and apply a remedy that soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, uncover the sight and put on its face an orilliet to cover for some days, and always keep it in a dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then leave the house little by little, and behave according to the patient's condition; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And one came to us who was from the Irach, who told us that in their country they did something called almagda, through which one draws water, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	 And these are the likenesses of the forms of Almagda, because those who do not recognize them may see them; and they should be properly of iron.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And their heads should have the same subtlety, and their ends in three sharp points.
de la char sor le neis	 on flesh over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes hairs appear on the nose in various forms, some of which resemble many-legged scorpions; and there are those that have flesh with a reddish hue, and others with fair skin tone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In this case, then, for the hairs that are fair and not reddish, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and throw the oil on those hairs, and pull them out; then cut what you can with a sharp, subtle scalpel, until you know that all the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with all the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if there is swelling or an abscess, then provide relief as needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize until the blood is dried up and all the matter is removed, then cast in the nose easily and vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nose bleeds and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not come out as needed, know that there is matter born in the bone above, which prevents the instruments from cutting: then you must insert a thread of linen about a thumb’s width thick, and let it be knotted by hand, and have between each knot a distance of a finger or less; and let the patient place the end of the thread into his nostril as much as he can, and pull through the nose until it comes out through the mouth into the throat; and many times children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for those who wish to do it; then hold with one hand the end that comes out of the nose, and with the other hand the end that comes out of the mouth, and know each after the other by following the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then draw out the thread, wipe off the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian unguent, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for III days or more, until the unguent has dissolved all that remains of the flesh; and then put a lead plug in the nose for some days until it heals, and if dry medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to clean out the head, into which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a plug, and the conduit likewise; and if you wish, make it a closed plug, and let the instrument be full to clean out the head; and have one handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 of the skin on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 often appears on the tip of the nose a disease called "telul", and grows and becomes very large, to the point that it is a visible thing to look at; and therefore you must cut it at the beginning, and remove all its force, then apply the cautery or burning medicine on the spot; and if you delay cutting until it is large, beware if it is hard, of a purple color, of poor condition: do not touch it with iron because it is an incarnate abscess, for when one cuts it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of purple color, and you see that it can be completely cut, let the patient empty themselves and cut without fear, and treat the place with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 When the nose is cut and pierced
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution for continuing work comes into one of these cartilages, it benefits little, except in some men.
