Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is therefore necessary that when this happens to someone, one should see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together in a seam, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from one side or the other, then you must cauterize all the parts of their heart until they heal, then join the two lips together in a seam, and bandage them, and sprinkle on powder of dragon's blood and ground incense; and put on the powders a piece of strong emplaster or another adhesive emplaster, and let it remain until it falls off by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 The manner of sewing is such that you join the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the abdomen; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	 of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many people get hard abscesses within the lips, resembling grains of peas, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and cut into each knot, and take it with tweezers and chop it in each part; then fill the place after cutting with vitriol powder until the wound is stained; and then the juice of asperum, and treat the place with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	 of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 Often appears on the gums a fleshy growth called «albulus» by the ancients; then you must hold it with tongs, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood flow; then apply on the place vitriol powder, or other powders that restrain and dry out; and if this flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize: it does not return after the cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	 of scurvy
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 Some are assembled at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; sometimes the teeth become black and yellow and rotten, until the decay reaches the gum, making the teeth stink; then you must make the patient sit in your lap, with his head resting on your chest, and scrape off the teeth or the scabs until nothing remains; do the same with the blackness and greenness, and with the yellowness and other spots, until they are completely removed; if one removes at the first attempt that which is there, it is good; but if not, then continue to scrape again on the second day and third, until you have removed everything; know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work shows, because the scrapers used for scraping outside the teeth have different forms than those used for scraping between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 It is necessary that when you cure the tooth of its pain you delay drawing it as long as you can, for this should not be done; for it is a very high substance until such time that there is no excuse for extracting it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is forced to have it drawn, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth that aches.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often the pain deceives the patient and thinks it is in a healthy tooth, and has a good tooth drawn; and still the pain does not depart because of this, until the bad one is extracted, for we have already seen this happen to these lords; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you cauterize all around the tooth with very strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or with fine forceps bit by bit, until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp the forceps, and let the patient's head be in your lap between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and gently push it into each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is perforated and rotten, then you must fill it with cloths where the holes are; and gently clamp it with tongs so that it does not break when clamping; and one must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take good care that you do not break it, leaving a part behind, and the patient will suffer greater pain from the root than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware not to act like the ignorant doctors, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the jaw, and do not bring what we have mentioned; but they often cause great illness due to the roots that remain, or because of the broken jaw, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is removed, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood flows there, which often happens, then fill the place with ground vitriol; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	 The forms of the instruments, with which one first removes the teeth, should be long and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 They should be made of strong material so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made of good iron, and they should have teeth to hold fast.
de la racine des dens	 from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after pulling, you must put cotton moistened in butter on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the spot is softened, then put in the pincers called "algefri", with which the tooth seems like a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and that is the form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not come out with all these tweezers, then it is necessary that you uncover all the flesh around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", that is to say pincers, in this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 And let it be outside and large so that it does not break. And if the root jumps out this way, it is good. If not, then help yourself with all the instruments, whose shapes are shown here below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And one helps oneself with this instrument that has two branches, as is shown in this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 And other irons which are found at the base of the teeth, and this instrument which resembles large tweezers, as is shown in this form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 And let this instrument be such that it cannot break, and know that many instruments for teeth are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master subtil finds his instrument by himself according to what his works and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where the ancient ones did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of all things. And if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, where it can be done, then he looks for the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and he helps with gestures, here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can hold and remove it; and then restore with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone and it is small, this instrument can extract it all.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 Quant les dents apparaissent pas selon la nature du corps, et leur forme est laid, et surtout chez les jeunes femmes, il faut savoir si la dent est née après la dent, et n'est pas à sa place correcte, et on ne peut ni la broyer ni la limer : alors, l'arracher ; et s’il y a de l'air avec la dent, alors prend cet instrument dont voici la forme, et il ressemble à un petit bec, et soit en fer indien aigu en sommet.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the pliers take little by little in your hands day by day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it seems that it can be filed down, then file it with such a file as is shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 And it is like the file on which one makes needles; and with a file, day by day lightly in hand, so that it does not move until it falls out; then the plain at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then you must file the roughness until it is even, so that it no longer hurts the tongue or corrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	 When the tooth falls out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth fall out, either from a blow or from falling, and the patient cannot bite into what he eats without them falling out, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, but that does not work; then they must be restrained by a golden thread, for a silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the width of the space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the loose teeth, as many as there are, until you reach wisely to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the wrapping again up to the place where you started, and gently and wisely tighten your hand so that it does not move; and let your knot be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then cut the heads of the wire with a pair of pliers, and join them together, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put it in such a way that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it so tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose, or the wire breaks, then hold it with another wire; and it will remain and serve thus for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the 2 healthy teeth, and the 2 molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and skilled, and sometimes one makes the shape of a cow bone tooth, and puts it in the place where there is a lack, and holds it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 Of copper to cleanse the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Any time this ligament comes from under the tongue by nature, so that one is born thus; or by accident due to a healed wound; and the operation is such that you open the mouth of the patient and let his head rest in your hand, and raise the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is due to a healed wound, then push the hook and cut that ligament wide; and ensure that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery underneath; and when you have done this, raise the place with rose water and aloes, or cold water, then put under the tongue a linen compress; and let the patient rinse each night, so that the place cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding continues, place a vitriol poultice on the spot; and if the blood flow weakens, cauterize with a slow cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with another treatment until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and if you see the flesh change to black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it turns to pus and there is moisture, apply onion juice, and make a fine slit with a lancet, and cleanse it from both sides; and if the blood flow weakens during your work, place a vitriol poultice until it is dried up, then return to your work until you draw out all the pus; then lift the flesh gently and carefully, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	 Of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes there are abscesses in the throat called "glands," and they are properly called the two tonsils. When you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and of dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent bleeding; but let it be until it is dead, and then you will divide it, or it would burst on its own; and if it is of white color again, and the root is thin, have ready the instrument to cut, but first check if the abscess is hot and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his eyes be in your shadow, and he opens his mouth and you take the instrument between your hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, of which here is the form; and let it be of silver or fine bronze like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take a probe and fit it in the almond, and draw it strongly above as much as you can; and draw something from the tissues along with it, then cut with the instrument, of which here is the form, resembling pincers; however, the heads are curved, one next to the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then borrow it with pincers, here is its form.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 And let it be sharp on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water and water and honey, and if blood continues to flow, then gargle the patient with water in which pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves have been boiled, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then continue the treatment until it is cured. And sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them as well in the same manner.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say the abscess of little sense; and it had almost closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so high that it had pushed out two bones through the two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened immediately, and inserted a stiletto into one of the openings, then drained out the pus, and removed a large portion of bone; then I did the same in the other nostril opening, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the stiletto into the abscesses, and drained some of it, but only a little blood came out; and thus the throat passage of the woman was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease cutting from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing again, filling the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I cauterized it inside the throat: so it remained without growing; and I left those parts, entrusting her to God.
de l’uve	 of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When pus descends into the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is beneath, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, and you see that the aforementioned abscess is calmed down, and it is subtle, then you should cut it; and this one which is round gathered and not long; and it is bloody or of ash color or black, then you should avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned before; then insert the awl into the eye, and draw it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments which I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it injures the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and care for it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then you must use ingenuity in the cauterization to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of cautery should be sharp and keen.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient should place their head in your hand, and then press their tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and apply sharp, lively vinegar, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which looks like this:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And there should be on the head a tuft where one puts the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and wound; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press on the eye for half an hour, until you see it is numbed and the biting of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with all the cotton into the channel above, so that the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfected, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four or five days. And if you need to repeat the cautery of the medicine, then repeat it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse it with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 This cure is more effective than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camphor and hyssop and marjoram and rue and chamomile and mugwort and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them in a pot, and put ashes in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well covered with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument made like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be of silver or copper, and one of its ends should be inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapor reaches the eye through the tear duct, until the eye is inflamed; then repeat this often until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, because many things can happen; and do not do this unless at the end of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a dog and place inside its head an eggshell, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to irritate the mouth, and it is a good remedy along with the salt.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 Often a bone or fishbone gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must extract what you can see. Press the patient's tongue against the instrument under the sun until you see movement. And that which does not open and remains lodged in the throat, you should make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps it will come out with the vomiting. If the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of apple, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread, tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it. When it reaches its place, it will expand and you can pull it out; if it does not come out with what we have said, take a lead instrument of this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 And let the instrument be curved at the top so that it may more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised upwards; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest it come into view, nor push any bone inside; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows where the thing is difficult; thus he pushes it down, where he draws it strongly through all the instrument equally, until it passes.
de la sansue de la gorge	 of the phlegm of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the phlegm is treated with medicine, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when that does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, after you have pressed the tongue to the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the blood, draw it with the smallest hook, or with subtle tongs that are suitable for this task.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if this does not work, take a heated iron wire, and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert a hot iron into the hollow of the wire, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient becomes thirsty all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the patient's mouth, and pour it in without gulping, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not stop as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the tool I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without hesitation.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot with visible charcoal, and let the lid be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and through this hole place the head of the instrument; then pour your fumigation into it, and have the patient put the head of the reed in their mouth, and close their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but comes up to the blood vessel; and the blood will fall now, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient endure thirst, and eat salty things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for her to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	 And the form of the instrument with which one draws blood is such that, when it can be seen, it resembles curved pincers to enter into the throat; and it should have the likeness of a hawk's beak, and there should be roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	 the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many types of abscesses are, as recalled hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways that one is exactly like the other, and from which it draws moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is according to the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 Car the abscess on the head is different from that at the base, and the fleshy abscess is different from that which occurs in the joints, and each should be judged accordingly in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that should not be incised until the head is mature according to its development; and there are those which must be incised when they are ripe and do not die according to their maturity, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 Because when an abscess occurs near the joints and it is left until it is rotten around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contracture in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 When the abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it is mature, it will harm the main limb; when it is near the anus, perforate it as soon as it is ripe; and it is not appropriate to perforate a ripe abscess before digestion is complete, except for that which is near the anus, lest it putrefy in depth, become elongated inside, and a fistula develops; and it cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And it is necessary that you know the hour of perforation of the abscess which has ripened according to completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and redness, and the discussion and preparation of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you place the perforation in the most dependent part of the abscess, where it opens up; and let the perforation be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there are no folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before this, the body will be filled with its poison, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the edges and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And you should bring in small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cauterize, and cover; when they have become as thick as cloths, and are dead, you should act as with blisters: and if there are such that are split into three corners, and if there are such that one cuts like the leaves of myrtle, like abscesses of the angles; and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar cutting.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head, like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again; do this many times from great to small, until all the pus comes out; likewise if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit may sometimes jump with the issue of the pus, which can accidentally kill the patient, and you would not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have noticed your abscess, cleanse the wound, and observe if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, bring tenths of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must insert into each one a tent so that they touch against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of skin, and you have taken it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and cure with oiling until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold and clear water, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, bring management and care, and the powders that I have mentioned earlier in this book. If it is in winter and the place where the abscess is is very sensitive, you must apply tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil; and if it is in summer and the place is fleshy, you must apply cloths soaked in water or cold wine and oil, for three days as we have said. Then lance the abscess and clean and treat it until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 And this must be recognized universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	 of pustules
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where pimples come on the head, and are like us who have them in clusters, just like the spines of a hedgehog, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fat and like those where there is moisture such as marrow; and there are some that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the art does not interfere.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is such that you should test with all the instruments that are called "entromissoire," from which the forms come hereafter, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Car if it contains moisture, then open it from above the long [bone].
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape off without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left there; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will heal what remains of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure that nothing remains of the night; then heal the wound with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess is large, cut it according to this form, lengthwise; and cast your onions therein, and scrape all around, and put all your effort into drawing out the cloth where it lies; and if the art of healing does not comply, then do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And likewise treat the abscess if it is hard, and in cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut above the hard and moist abscess, for it is lighter because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if any of these abscesses have no moisture at the tip, like the one I cut from the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess hard, rough, and white, and it could not be broken; and had anyone struck it, they would have wounded her as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 En others abscesses coming to the head, except for those which come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place, so that the pus may exit; and care for them as is necessary.
des scrophules	 Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often these abscesses occur at the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin; sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body and are numerous, interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is specifically within its own rib, like the nut and the head abscess, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In this one, therefore, that you see of good disposition to touch, and it is similar in color to the body, and it moves from each part and is not harsh on the nerves of the neck nor on the artery or vein, and it is not deep; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape each part, and stretch the two lips of the heart to the ears, if you need to, as we have said in the abscesses of the head; and draw little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula not be too sharp or cutting, lest the hand slip, and do not go too far forward, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that staunch blood, and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood is staunched, return to your work until you complete it; then seek with your finger if there remain any small scrofula, and cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a great vein in the root of the scrofula, then it is not fitting that you cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut all the scrofula, then it is necessary that you join the two lips of the wound, and sew them immediately, since there should be no delay due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 then it is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it, and pulling strongly, and sewing as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulae that hold superfluity, pierce them where they appear to be dead; and pierce them in the same way as those previously mentioned, in descending order, then apply bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with ointments containing animal fat, until it heals.
de squinance	 from the shoulder
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 The ancients spoke and discussed the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is a record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 For those who have shoulder pain, it is necessary that the slit in the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided; and do not use this method because all the veins and the pomp of the patient are hot with abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the disease is in the channel of the pomp (throat), it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid death by strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four, a small transverse cut between two circles or according to the size of the syphac fissure, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat to all the bone, then split the heart until it reaches the trachea; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the hypoglossal nerve as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the trachea which jumps out through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the hour has passed in which one fears strangulation, gather together the two lips of the heart wound, and sew them up alone without a bandage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasis said that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and there is a lack of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, which passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young woman took a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the cartilage of the larynx; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had come out of it, even though it had not struck a vein or artery, but rather the windpipe, and the air was exiting strongly through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed the wound, treating it until it was healed; and all that happened to the maiden was that she lost her voice, which later returned to normal; therefore, I say that in cutting the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	 of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess the color of jet, and it is very common in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; in the natural kind there is no venom.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accident is according to two manners, of which one resembles us grease, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it should not be worked on to make a fire except in the small one, and prove and search all the intromissary: if you find it like our grease, and it does not open to any vein, then cut it off, as we cut the nose, and draw out all its hair, if there is any; and examine well soon, and treat it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	 of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways are of us, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I speak of all the differences that exist between us and the exit.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 I say that the flow is hot and feverish while the inflammation lasts, until the suppuration is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With this knot there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own bag and corresponds to the body's color, and begins like a blister, and grows large; and they are of two kinds, either dry or moist, and many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 When you come to the care of the knot, it is necessary that you test and inquire first with all the instruments called "entromissoires," according to what its form will be in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 Et la manière d'examiner les abcès pour nous est que tu prennes le lieu le plus humide que tu trouves dans l'abcès, et tourne tes doigts peu à peu, jusqu'à ce que tu saches que l'instrument ait percé le cœur, puis selon la grandeur de l'abcès; ensuite, retire l'instrument, et fais attention à ce qui sort.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 Se l'humidité qui court à la surface a une couleur, perce-la comme je l'ai dit pour les autres abcès; et si après avoir retiré l'instrument, de l'humidité en sort, sache que c'est gras. Donc, fais-en une croix, prends-le avec des pincettes, et écorche légèrement chaque côté, et fais attention à la couche où il repose pour que tu le traies proprement avec l'aiguille; et si tu ne peux pas le traire proprement, alors coupe-le en morceaux jusqu'à ce qu'il n'en reste plus rien.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 Car if there remains anything, the nose returns by many times; and if a little remains, and the blood coagulates, fill the wound with some corrosive powders, and close the wound, and apply soothing things to the hot abscess, and treat with other treatments until it is healed; and if the nose is large, sew the two lips of the wound, and treat those who eat flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 and if the vein is beating against you or another, then hasten and fill the place with a solution of vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound festers and the bleeding subsides; then return to what remains of the nose.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the forms of the intermittent instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula; and they are like the needles with which one sews shirts, and they are made of citrin bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more, and they are more proven with black lead to surround the curves of the fistula; and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of the onions are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are onions that have two curves of three types also; and there are onions that have three curves, and they are of three types also; and there are onions that have two curves, and single-curved onions, which are of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these instruments are cutting, and there are such that cut only from one side, with which one can scrape the nails without cutting into the vein or nerve; and among these implements are the retractors attached to handles, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they come in three types: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are used only on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the scrapings of figs, according to this form, with which one stops bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 and it is sometimes placed at the site that heals quickly the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes they come according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to decay, to such an extent that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, he must follow this form according to these lines from line .b. to line .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine that renews flesh, then join the two lips of the wound together with stitches, and continue the treatment until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down and is softened by its size as happens to women, then make two cuts in the upper part, through two similar slits; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line .b. to this line .g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and introduce what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	 Of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	 These abscesses that come under the armpits are hard like scrofula with ribs, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with a suitable ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, incise it as we have said for the incision of scrofula, and if the wound lets out pus, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	 of artery breakage
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it is closed, it often results in abscesses. The same happens with a swollen vein and abscess; and you recognize it this way when it is due to the artery, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel tightness; and when it is due to the vein, the cause is evident; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the nails or in the angles or at the neck or in many other places, and it is very large.
