Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is therefore necessary to avoid the iron cure, and the one at the head must also be avoided, and in the case of an artery swelling, make a long incision above the skin; then work the cut with scissors, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered; then insert underneath it a needle, and make it pass through to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then stitch the place between the two threads with an intromitter until the pus comes out, and let the abscess be relieved; then apply the cure as before, so that the thread falls off; then treat it as for a wound, until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the vein cut, it is necessary that you dye your hand with what you can from the abscess all over the skin, then insert the needle underneath the place you hold in your hand, and make it pass through, and let there be a double thread, so that you draw it out on the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have said, with the thread of one of the two parts at the two ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then insert another needle all along one thread underneath the entire abscess at the first incision of the needle, and constrict the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the superfluity comes out, then cut the superfluity of the skin and leave what is bound; then put on a cloth moistened with wine and oil, then apply treatments of bandages and dressings until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	 of the nerves' abscesses
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Similarly, just as abscesses can occur in the artery and vein, they also occur in nerves when they are struck or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens most often in the shoulders and arms, and in all places where there are joints, and it is a very severe abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many positions without pain; and when it is pressed hard, then the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely within the flesh, but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, or up or down, and those that are in joints must not be struck with iron: perhaps there would be contraction; and those that are on the head or forehead, open the skin to a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with pincers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it on the edge of the nail, and scrape it off, then remove it and close the wound with stitches, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	 of hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in the belly and not elsewhere, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, with subtle roots and large heads; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were already split open, and moisture always flowed out of them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I cut them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces and the other six. And the work in the incision is such that you should consider if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of a subtle root; then you should cut with a wide spatula, and let the cauterizer be in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in cutting often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the wound overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made thread of linen and tie up the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not stop restraining the linen thread until it cuts off the artery, and each one without any effort; and if the roots are thick, there is fear of cutting at once for the abdomen, but you can well cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the vein which is of dark color and poor sense and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 Car it is an infected abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the abscess hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	 When the wound is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the wound comes from cautery of the skin or splitting of sinew, and is on the belly or in some wounds as it happens in other places, whether it is blood from veins or arteries according to what was said before, or from inflammation; and if it is through the splitting of sinew and exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a minor thing without pain, and opens from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed between two fingers it springs back, and then returns, and by chance it may become hardened, and greatly increases with hot baths and intense effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it appears well when you press it in your hand, do not constrain at all; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess appears by these signs as large and hard, and it is fixed according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, then it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you must see if the appearance is for the blood of the artery, or vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 Then you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is for the intestine or bladder, then you must instruct the patient to tie his leg, and be stretched straight, then seal all around the bag; then command him to lie quietly between your hands, then go around the place that you have sealed with all the linen cloth, then extend half of the abscess above all the great knuckle; then tie it around with a strong thread or with a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot of the ligature be tight; then work half of the abscess stretched over the ligature, and put your index finger in, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught by the ligature, then untie it, and push the intestine out of the stomach; and if you find the bladder, then take it with the knuckle, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, then go well around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads in them, and put the two needles around that which you have made crosswise that you make perforate; then press the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it rots, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or you cut it when it has softened and rotted, then cure of what is necessary, and take away the abscess as we have said; and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as is necessary, and sew up the place.
dou chancre	 of the cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 We have said in the division the resemblances of cancer, and how one must work on it with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and we say that cancer infects the flesh, and great care is needed in the cure, and the ancients said that when cancer is in a place where it can be scraped off, like cancer which is in the breast, and in the thigh, and in similar places, and one should remove all of it when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, then one should not approach it, for I have never known anyone to heal from it; nor has anyone ever healed from it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile some time; then make him vomit if he has manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good place to do the work; then cast your eyes on the cancer, and the hair from all sides, and remove it from all sides leaving nothing behind; and let the blood flow strongly, and press well the place with your hand or with something else, and if the bleeding makes you fear the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stanched; then cure with another cure until he is cured.
de ydropisie	 of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 we have already spoken of the similarities to dropsy, and in what manner the gathering of water is done, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is made by medicine, and that which is cured by iron; only eclites are cut; and one should not touch iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, for they are deadly things; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called «eclites» with medicine, and the cure does not profit, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as swelling of the belly and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient to be of strong constitution, and he has no other illness but dropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus: lift the patient upright in your hands, and the assistant presses the belly from behind, expelling the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the spiked spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 and let it be pointed, yet not so deep that when inserted it can reach the intestines or injure them; then check if the dropsy is towards the intestines: if so, your incision should be on the right side of the navel below the umbilicus, three fingers wide; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the navel; and if it is due to kidney problems, it should be on the right. And it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluidities do not flow to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it in, and lift your hand along the entire thickness between the skin and the fat as if scraping to a thickness of one nail or around; then pierce the fat until the thickness comes to the watery place, which is the place of the water, then draw out strongly, and pour this instrument whose form is thus:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a fine silver cane, and it is of light brass or bronze, and has in the lower part a small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision with which the scribe cuts the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 on the tip above is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it rises now on the instrument; empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than is needed in that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the release of his spirit by the weapon, or he falls fainted, or approaches death; but empty according to the amount of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient indicate, and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now for the cork that stops the hole which is on the vase, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then begin again with the instrument the next day, if you see the patient enduring this, and draw a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to empty until there remains but a little bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient and you leave much water in him, cure him with hot sepulture or sand, and by much sweating or bathing in the sun, and let him drink wine; and cure him with desiccative medicines until he is dry, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 of the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or with a small opening, or the opening is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it should be done immediately by piercing all around the most subtle part of the glans according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then place in the opening a thin plug of linden, and tie it and hold it thus for three days or four. And when he wants to urinate, then remove the plug, and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out freely does not require closing.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 He whose opening is small should be treated with the linden plug as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are injured, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate forward unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot engage in sex because the matter cannot reach the womb, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then stretch the head of the penis and the foreskin like the width of a feather's quill, so that the opening comes in the middle, as it should; and beware of bleeding that occurs frequently, and if it happens, staunch it with what staunches blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	 of the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many times these abscesses come in the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; some are malignant, others not; so it is necessary that you take them at one time, subtle, and cut and clean all, then put on a moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment; then cure with the ointment definitivum until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the bath is malignant, of foul color and stinking, then you must bring a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cut it, and if the bath is partly on the stick and partly inside the skin, then you must first remove the part of the bath that is inside; and when it is healed, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you treat them together, it is not certain that the head of the stick will not be perforated, and blackness and corruption come into the stick and the joint; then all that is black and corrupt must be cut away, then apply the plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranates and beans, then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if there is a flow of blood, then apply the lunar cautery according to this manner:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery helps in two situations together: that is to say, for bleeding and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must insert into the urethra a leaden cannula, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair is thick at the head of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or if there is a wound or abscess, then you must scrape with one instrument until the skin is freed, and the head of the penis is released from all sides; and if it is difficult to describe this, then you should scrape with one spatula some at the head of the penis and the skin; then cut well between the two, and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water there, so that it does not thicken again.
de la circoncision	 of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 Circumcision is not a separation of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work by our will and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, the lightest for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 Because I have seen most of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions around Al-Dal (Old Dal, perhaps a reference to an ancient city or region), and they did so with force and all at once; thus, the heart fled because there are two layers, and by chance if one cuts the upper layer, the lower one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 And there the patient recovers consciousness, and the pain is doubled, and in the amputation of the finger, the point of the member is not assured; and in the amputation of the nail perhaps the iron slips away, and the work is ruined, and many times it happens that they do not need amputation, which I intended.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 From the amputation done with forceps on all the ligament of the finger, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forceps cut exactly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because when you press your hand and cut equally on all sides at the same time; but let the thread be well tightened around the skin; and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if it understands, that you are only doing to tie the thread around the finger, then let it rest in all the ways you can; then hold it straight between your hands, and return the forceps between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the finger and blow into the heart, and pull it up until the head of the finger comes out; then clean it well of the accumulated dirt, then bind the place tightly with a double thread, then tie another ligature below the first one; and hold it with two fingers by the second ligature at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then raise the heart quickly and pull out the head of the finger; then let the blood flow little by little, because that is the mother; and put powder on top and a cloth glued with a mixture of a cooked egg yolk tempered with rose water, made with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and continue to care for it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The shape of strength for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be sharp and cutting, and the heads should be as large as the little finger equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 The mistake in cleansing is when the head inside flees the incision; therefore, you must extend it to your fingernail, so that the place does not become an abscess; and also cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with tongs, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 And if it exceeds three days, and what is under the foreskin is swollen, then let it be until the abscess is calmed down, and lightly scrape off the scab; then cut as you can move, and take care of the part of the foreskin, so that nothing harms it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Cure the place of sudden wounds with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if the cut is deeper than necessary and it goes too deep, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 of retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is caused by a stone, or congealed blood, or a bone, or a piece of flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; and let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and let the patient restrain himself as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constricted to express the stone upward, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument which is called "syringe," and here is its shape: and let it be of fine silver, thinly hammered, like the feather of a bird; and let its tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie at the end a bag of wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the superfluity of the wool and put it to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a seat, and wash the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then place the syringe gently into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the scrotum; then push the syringe forward until the bladder, and the patient feels it coming to the empty space, and this is not done according to this order except because the passage through which it goes is twisted; then draw out all the wool bit by bit, and the urine follows the wool, then remove the syringe, and allow the urine to flow; and recommence the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When the bladder is scalded by blood or there is a collection of pus within it, you should infuse water and medicines. Do this with the entire instrument called "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed and has three holes: two on one side and one on the other, as you see. And let the place where the medication passes be such that it tightly seals the tube without additional material, so that the moisture can be drawn out and injected when needed. And when you infuse your medications into the bladder, put the end of the syringe in the liquid, and pull on the plunger; thus, you will draw the liquid into the syringe, and then push it strongly back in; thus, the liquid will enter inside and reach the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it. This is the form of the subtle enema used to enema the bladder: and here it is: 123
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and below at the breast where the ribs fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture with which you wish to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a double thread of good linen, and heat the pouch containing the moisture over the fire; then insert the nozzle of the enema into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder so that all the moisture enters gradually, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it neatly around; then pass a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like a bucket, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 We have already said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction along with medicines; and I have told the difference between the stone in the kidneys, and all the signs, and on what kind of stone one must work with the incision; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 I say that the stone which is caught in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine flows from the bladder like fine water; and there is blood, and the patient's penis hurts, and he urinates frequently, and then it stops; and many times the root of this occurs; and the healing of children is light until they are four years old, and it is very grave for the elderly, and it is in the middle way, for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with a clyster, in order to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For sometimes it hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet, and throw him backwards and downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it goes up from its place; then let him sit between your prepared hands, and let his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then seek and touch within; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall with the touch of all, then moisten your finger in oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent; and put it into his fundament, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press on top of your finger, and expel it out where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand under the scrotum, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the scrotum in the part where the incision is made; then insert the spatula covering, which is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it goes between the thighs and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the vein; and let it be straight onto the stone, and your two fingers should always be on the anus, and let the cut across be so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the finger in the anus will make it come out without effort; and know that there are such stones with angles and edges: it is difficult to remove; and there is such which is beneath, similar to a hazelnut, and round, whose removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 To that which has angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, then you must extract with tweezers that are like a file at the tip, to firmly grasp the stone so that it does not escape; or you insert a subtle instrument curved at the tip beneath; and if you cannot manage in this way, then widen the opening of the bladder, and if the urine is turbid, then constrain with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first place the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut it, then pull it out strongly, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, then it must be sewn, making a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes out continuously through the place where the wound cannot be closed; but nevertheless, you must strive to pull it out or break it with pincers until you draw it out piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bandage it, and put on top a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the hot abscess; then let the patient rest on his pillow, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et quant tu le desliies, so well wash the place with oil and water, then treat it with a dressing of diaphoretic ointment and basil-based ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if the wound develops abscesses or corrosions, and a clot of blood in the bladder that retains urine in such a manner that it is passed with the urine: then put your finger in the wound and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will damage the bladder and make it rot; then lift the wound with water and ashes and salt, and assist him in all ways you know until he is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you bind his two thighs together and apply the medicines on the spot.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra of the penis, and fixed inside, and urine cannot come out; then the treatment for this that I say is as follows: cut it many times, and he is relieved from pain by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven this so.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take an iron rod according to this shape, and let it be fixed with three prongs on one stake:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the rod into the penis lightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand against the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will come out immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is immediately broken, and it urinates with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread below the stone and another above, then make an incision near the stone between the two threads, then extract the stone, untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and heal the patient until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	 of the female stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 It rarely happens that a stone is lodged in women, and if it ever does happen, the treatment is difficult and hindered by three things: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to reveal herself to doctors, especially when she is modest.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is such that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-versed in this hand art; and the fourth manner is such that the stones of the woman are more deeply embedded than those of the man, which requires a deeper cut, and there is great fear involved. And if necessity demands it, you must take a wise midwife, and one can scarcely find her, and if you cannot find her, then do not seek a subtil male physician; rather present a wise old woman who knows something about the art of life in women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command that she perform what you order for the investigation of the stone; and look very carefully to see if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she must press it under her finger, and recommend that she insert her finger into the malaide's vagina, and seek and press her left hand strongly onto the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, then she must move it from the entrance of the bladder downwards until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike against the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the anus, where it is more easily moved, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then push the thread into the incision, if you feel the stone, tighten the wound so that the stone can come out strongly, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you know the similarities to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the blood overcomes you, apply powdered vitriol to the spot, and hold it there for an hour until the blood is stanched; then return to your work until the stone is weakened, and have the instruments I mentioned to you in the extraction of stones from men to help you in your work; and if the blood overcomes you, and it is from the artery that has been cut, apply powder to the spot and bind it with cloths and bandages, and do not attempt this again, but leave the stone and do not remove it, for the patient might die by chance; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the place is cold, return to your work until the stone is weakened.
de hernie carnouse	 About hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 About hernia aqueous, it is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white sap under the heart of the kidney, which contains the egg; and it is called "sap", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the kidney between the white sap that we have said. And these do not happen unless there is a pustule.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the generation of this hernia comes from weakness in the kidneys, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it comes from a blow to the kidneys, and this moisture has many colors: it is yellowish like jaundice, or redless, black, or white and watery, and this happens more; these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is in the white sap that we have said, then the abscess is reasonable, a long pustule like the shape of an egg, and the kidney does not open, because it has moisture all around. 》
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess swells with a part of the egg, and therefore it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the leather of the cushion and the white silk, one can feel it well; thus when you want to know the color of the moisture, test all the introduced instrument, from which the form is made before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 According to what follows the instrument, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we heal it with fire, it is necessary for the patient to be bled according to his ability and the fullness of his body; then make him sit on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs of the chest of the cushion; then take the spatula knife, and cut the leather of the cushion in the middle lengthwise down to near the shoulder, and let your cut be straight while cutting the leather of the cushion until it reaches white silk, and peel it delicately according to your ability; then pierce the silk full of water through a large hole, and drain all the water, and then place your fingers, and stretch the silk upwards; and do not touch the chest of the cushion, but only the silk; cut all or in pieces likewise the side of him delicately, that if you do not cut wisely, the water will return; and if the egg jumps out of your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work of the silk; then join the two lips of the chest of the cushion with a stitch, then cure him as the other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the ion to all the suspensory, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if water is collected in two parts together, know that these are two veins; then cut the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound wool soaked in rose oil; and put outside other wool soaked in wine and oil, and put on top of the two ions, and put on top doubled cloths, and tie it all up with the ligature according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths, and fill them with wool shreds according to this pattern and sew them together at the top of the breeches, and one of the heads takes from the waist up to the back, and the other on the wrist; and the other two heads on the two angles, and all the assembly is tightened in the loop of the breeches; sometimes this ribbon for cautery is used instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take a thin surgical cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we have said, so that the white layer containing water is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that layer at the corners, and peel with this hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cauterization in all ways that you can, until you burn everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more beneficial; and change your behavior regarding blood loss, and change the actions of cutting; and if anything goes against you, such as abscess or bleeding or other things, then treat what goes against you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure because of its horror, then administer perforation, as I tell you. When you are certain through the indications that we have mentioned that aquous humour is present there, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part to the full extent of your finger width, and insert the perforation into the body cavity; and let the hole be wide so that all the liquid can flow freely. Then place cotton on the spot, bind it, and leave it for the remaining water to drain. Then treat until the wound is healed. And if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out of the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or an instrument used to draw water from dropsical patients; the form of which is mentioned above. Widen the hole in the wound, and know that the water will return and be collected after six months or thereabouts. And when it is collected as before, the patient will pass his days thus.
de l’aposteme des coions	 from an abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the incision of this vein there is more fear in many situations, for which it seems to me better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the operation and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	 I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and especially to the testicles; and this is in very many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 This is to say, due to the spreading of sharp and acute excess humors to the testicles, or from blows; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the body's color; and no pain is found, but it is a serious abscess. And sometimes it is dangerous, perforating, and purulent, with a reddish color, and sometimes it comes from a knot in an artery, or from a swelling of veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is due to the swelling of an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it against your fingers; and one must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 He who is affected by the swelling of a vein is known by its disposition to change color upon touching with fingers, and one can well make an incision on this resemblance, and on other parts; and it is that you cut the heart of the testicles, then raise the egg upwards, and draw out the white forcefully, and free the suspending membrane from all around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already hardened with these parts born, it is then necessary that you draw out the egg and cut it; and if there is air in the white, or within the vessels, it is necessary that you free all this membrane, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	 And if the base of the flesh is at the back, then you must cut all of it, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when your work is done, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then care for it with other remedies until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess wrapped in a covering like a bud, accompanied by the softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when he walks; and the cure for this illness is almost as dangerous as the previous one, but nevertheless we will tell you the work for it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a high seat, then put the suspender of the testicles down to your thighs, including all the vessels near the penis, and hold them tightly, and stretch them well; then cut with a sharp spatula wide across the vessels, until they are exposed, and then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle where it has two threads, and tie it first to the place where the vein came out, and tie it again to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as the others where one joins the bow, so that no vessel spills over which nourishes one of the testicles; for by this no harm comes, and if to all the vessels comes vein, it is necessary to draw the testicles to all the vessels; so that the bird does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	 From the fracture of the jaw
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The onset of this rupture is from the section that occurs in the jaw or the stretching over the stomach in the area of the hips, causing the intestines to descend from this fracture into one of the testicles; and this fracture is either in the jaw or from the stretching of it, and these two types come from many causes: from striking, jumping, roaring, lifting heavy loads, and similar things; and the sign that it is from the stretching of the jaw is that it happens little by little over a long time, and does not happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the bottom because the jaw presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	 And the sign is that it comes from the section of the liver, which at the beginning causes sudden pain, and the abscess has diverse appearances, close to the skin, and this is due to the exit of the intestines and the body away from the liver.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	 And sometimes the intestines descend with it and are retained therein, causing the patient to suffer great pain, especially when pressed upon.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	 And in these iron cautery treatments due to fear, which is why one must avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;
