puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the manner of this work is such that you instruct the patient to reach in with his hand into the wound if he can enter it; then place a bandage around his neck, and lift his thighs; then draw the intestines upwards, and cut all the skin from the testicles lengthwise; then insert your fingers of the tail into the groin according to what you need to open the wound, so that the intestines may exit; then skin the liver that is under the skin of the testicles, until the white liver remains uncovered on all sides; then insert your finger in that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white liver that is under the skin of the egg, and between the second liver; and then separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second liver; and then move to the right hand inside the groin of the testicles, and draw the white liver upwards to your left hand, and lift the egg with all the liver towards the groin; and instruct the attendant to raise the egg upwards, and untie that which is tied behind the binding; and check with your fingers if there is any part of the intestine wrapped in the hard white liver, and if you find anything, push it down into the abdomen below; then take a needle where there are I thick thread made of X threads, and insert it in the rear part of the liver, which is after the skin of the testicles, behind the groin, then cut the knots that appear from the threads, so that there are IVI threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the liver, of which we have spoken which is under the skin of the testicles, with a strong bondage of II parts; then wrap the knots of the threads, and bind them firmly with II parts, so that no servant who cares for him can enter through the mouths, where this aposteme may come; and put again the bondage according to the first long bondage of two fingers, and after these two bonds leave the liver under the groin of the testicles the width of a finger; and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the testicles, so that the veins and arteries run, as we have said before; then apply wet wool in oil to the wounds, and place the bandage that we have spoken of.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	 And sometimes the white surface is cauterized after incision due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this often happens and let the ligature remain until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling off, then apply a hot water poultice and place what we have said on top, until it falls off; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	 Of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	 In this situation I have never seen anyone who dared to treat with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done like the ligature which is tied with the vessel, in such a way that you tie the vessels after lightly lifting the skin below; then cut through the middle, and treat the abscess as we have described, until the vessel falls off; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Any time a hernia occurs in the groin, as we have said, it opens the place; and no one should cut into the intestines, and if they do, it is bad, and it heals every hour; and nevertheless, if it stays too long in this state, the wound or hernia grows so that the intestine comes out; and this happens due to the stretching of the hernia in the groin, as we have said, for it is stretched, then the place is softened and swollen and open; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured with an iron in this manner: and let the patient lie on their back between your hands, then cut the swollen place of the hernia wide according to the size of three fingers; and then extract the hernia that is under the skin as usual, then take a needle and place it on the apparent part of the hernia; and press deeply into the abdomen, then sew the two apparent parts of the hernia onto the head of the needle, and sew one and the other; then remove the head of the needle, and do not cut into the hernia or extend any other thing, as I have shown you in the cure of the intestine's hernia; then cure it with the cure for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, then cleanse and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	 The cautery is applied, and has no appearance in the incision, and the cauterization is moved to this place, and is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	 of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	 Often the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the membranes within are loosened, and it is easy to see; and it is necessary, when one wishes to cure it, that the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin onto the natural skin; then sew the two lips together with a single stitch, and if you wish, first sew the excess of the softened skin with three or four strong stitches; then cut between the stitches, and cure it as the other wounds, until it is healed, and let the threads fall.
dou chastrement	 Of the cautery
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that cautery is forbidden in our law, and therefore it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the physician knows how to respond when asked about it, and knows the treatment; and the other is that we often need to cauterize some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say therefore that cautery is done in two ways: by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the one that we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the joints are softened and relaxed; then take them with your hand until they are set and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Of tail castration: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspension, and strike each testicle with one blow, when they are well drained; and leave some of the subtle fat on the vessels; and this method of castration is milder than that done by attraction, because in attraction sometimes something remains of the testicles, causing the beast to desire lust; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	 Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 A hermaphrodite is in two ways among men: one way is that between the two testicles there appears as if by the nature of a woman, with hair, and sometimes urine passes through it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other way is in women, and it appears on the wrist like a wand and two tendons.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for men and women is that you cut all the hairs close, and treat it as other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	 of the tendon
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 The tendon is a close-cropped hair on the natural part, which is too unsightly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 You should dye the excess of the tendon with your hand or tweezers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest blood come out, then treat it like other wounds until it heals; and there is another hair that grows at the mouth of the womb, and fills up, and perhaps flows heavily, and looks like a cow's udder, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Si it is necessary that you cut [it], as we have said about the tendon, and treat [it] until it is healed.
de erratique	 of the tendon
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 Erratic [it] is when the woman's nature is not open, or the passage is small; it is natural from birth, or accidental due to illness that has come; whether it is caused by a narrowing of the vagina, or a subtle or thick cervix, and it is done deeply in the womb, or on the side, or below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly menstruation; and the knowledge of this is through the sight of the vulva.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the stupor is approaching, seek to your right or left hand.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is of subtle syphilis, and it is close to two pounds, then hurry; the course will be as follows: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, with her legs spread; then stretch out the two pounds very well, until the subtle syphilis is round and covered by the dressing; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman lie down each day, so that it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the syphilis is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a scalpel similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dressing is of new flesh, then suspend it with a hook and cut it; and have hemostatic medicines such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, along with plenty of egg; then apply a wide lead plate so that the wound cannot heal; and thus let it be for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when in the flesh comes a boil, then it must be covered in this manner, unless it is an infected abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an infected abscess that is in the flesh, one should not touch or do anything to it.
des emorroides	 of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually occur without cause, and when hemorrhoids are old, they become hard; and we have already said in the division their similarities, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and hard lumps, when they are embedded deeply in the flesh, and one does not feel them, then the treatment is not by cautery. xspace
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those who are at the mouth of the wound, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, it is necessary that you put the woman in a cold house; then apply the tweezers to the nipple and cut it at its roots; then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood flow, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then soak her feet against a wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is continuous bleeding, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and galls and similar things; then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make one poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if he faints, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If not, have him suck on cupping glasses at the back and breasts without piercing; then take wool, and soak it in juice of plantain or juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess has subsided, treat the place with onion until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp thistle, for this you must cover as I have said above; then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	 Of abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscess occur in the anus, such as chancres, purulent abscesses, herpes, styomiatae, fistulae, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Il is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess that comes to the bone, which is not one of those that form a boil; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is sharp at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it turns red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hasten to pierce, but let the abscess mature until the pain is relieved; and then have the patient sit on a stool, and place two small stools where he can lean back, and support his back, and bring his feet together at the sides of the leg; and let his thighs be spread apart, and have him put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then give him something to drink towards the left side, and bring to this side the instrument with which one works on the mouth of the abscess, from which comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument being brought, that you first insert the reed into the abscess to know its depth, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it is necessary that he put the horn of the instrument on top, and that he moisten the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and you make an incision in it with your hand gently, then you must cover it at the top with a poultice of fresh milk; and when the pustule is emptied, then you must place on the wound cloths moistened in rose oil or in dried green oil; and put the cloth over the wound to the bottom of the swelling, and put another one over the swelling and on the arm a clean linen cloth moistened in water where mallows have been cooked; then cure it after two days of greasing according to this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the swelling and the wound with an enema of water and honey, and then of water with lily roots and long-boiled arisotogelon; then return to greasing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is infected in the flesh, you must avoid using an iron cautery, but treat it as we have said in the section on healing.
de l’enfantement	 of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is first necessary for the midwife to recognize the natural form of childbirth, and the sign of this is when you see a woman pushing downwards and desiring to smell the air: then hasten the child to come out forcefully; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural form, and the issue is under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends onto its head, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the woman is purified of her superfluities by good purging; and those who come otherwise do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 Because it sometimes happens on his feet, and it comes upon the body or the head, and the hands, where it occurs on the belly or the buttocks, and by chance is turned onto his neck, and in other evil forms; therefore, it is necessary for the nurse that she be wise and skillful in these matters, and to guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	 If the child comes out on his head through natural birth, and the woman labors greatly, and her strength is weak, then let her sit upon a saddle, where the women hold her; and raise her nature with oil or cooked fenugreek, and then the nurse puts between his teeth the small spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And split the secondine, and cut to its fingernail so that the moisture inside comes out; and hold the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must enema the woman with fenugreek decoction mixed with sesame oil; then make her press and sneeze condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out strongly, then you must gently push them back bit by bit; and if they cannot go in, then place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up high; then knock over the seat onto the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall during the falling; and if the hand cannot go in, and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife mentioned before, and extract the child, and set it right.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the child's exit on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes on its feet, then you must push it upwards; and then turn it little by little, until it is even; then take one of the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 When he leaps up to his knees, then command him to take hold of it, and make it sneeze by conditioning; if it is stronger, then so be it, if God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	 And if he is not as strong as we have said, then turn him little by little, until he is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	 For then he is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if he does not come as we have said, then take mullein of altitude, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all together in a mortar; and put this ointment on the woman’s nature inside and outside; then make her sit in hot water up to below the ribs; and when she is well-soaked underneath, give her a drink of honey, and place it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child now leaps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	 Of the child's birth upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this manner, let the midwife put her hands little by little; then let it be supported on its neck, and let the feet hang down, and let it lie on the bed; and bend its hands little by little, and then take the hands up to the belly, and remove the cushions from below, until she is prepared; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them strongly, then move the belly upwards, then put your hands in; and take the child little by little; and instruct the woman to hold herself until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	 Of the issue of the child that comes with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to design a device to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then lay her on the bed and spread her legs widely; then introduce the muslin cloth that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then have her sit on a chair, and study to bring back the hand; and examine the child according to its natural form, and make it sneeze, and instruct her to grasp until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	 of the exit of the child onto its neck, and have its hands spread out, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the midwife touch her hand, then turn it little by little, and examine it gently; and when it is equal, place on top the natural muslin cloth with oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little; and when you have done this, have her sit on a chair, and instruct her to grasp; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	 By this same manner to all the secondary
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it comes out forcefully in this manner to all the secondary, cut the secondary with your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child turns on its face and on its neck, cut it from the navel so that it is not retained, and the child will die; then push the child back in until you have placed it as needed, and instruct the woman to take a breath: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	 of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	 Know that twins are born often, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are an extraordinary thing, and do not live, if at all; I know that they are multiplied by the siphon which divides them, which is attached to the navel; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one alone, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out badly, then treat it as we have said, and let the healer be skilled, and act quickly and lightly as she does; and act thus so that it moves to safety.
de plusors enfans	 of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 At times they are formed in the womb, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or many up to fifteen, and all are fully formed like children by the measure of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the healer know all these things, for perhaps similar things happen; so act accordingly as is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	 of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat the woman for a dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out on its own, and you are compelled to use your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; then let the woman be laid on her back, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the attendant holds a thread at two places where she lies on the bed so that she may not fall during the child's descent; then anoint the mouth of the womb with moist oil mixed with muscillaige of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then let the healer anoint his hands with these oils and these muscillaiges; then gently push them into the womb, then seek one place where she may push the hook that is suitable for this, and take care if the child is ready to descend on its head; then insert the hook into its eyes or neck or mouth or in some part of the palate or under the beard or in the groin or near the sides, and if the descent is on the feet, then insert it in the finger and in the middle of the ribs; and it is necessary that he hold the hook with his right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of his left hand, and gently push his whole hand, and insert the hook into any of these places that we have said, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then thrust one hook against the other, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then stretch them equally by moving from one side to the other, so that the hooks may come out, and let the hooks be sharpened to hold better, as shown in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if a part remains, then smear the ball of one of his fingers with oil and push it into that part, and pull out the other part; and if there is nothing left, then place this hook in a higher spot, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be pulled back due to tightness, then you must wrap it in a cloth until it all comes out; then cut off at the base of the foot or with a knife, and so you should do for the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow at the exit, or if there is a sharp angle in the forehead, then you must insert a thorny spatula between your teeth, and split the forehead and extract the sharpness; or you can use the instrument called "almidach," which comes with the instruments in the following chapter; and do the same if the child has a large natural head; then pull the bones with tongs, and if the head jumps out and is constrained by the pelvic brim, it should be split until the moisture that is in the worst exit can come out; and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if the belly or under the ribs is swollen, then you must pierce it until the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	 And if the child is standing on its feet, then the attraction is light, and the guidance to the mother's mouth is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is inverted in the belly or the breast, then you must extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and puncture the belly or the breast, until the moisture that is there runs out; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then push the heel of your hand into the depths of the mother's abdomen, and pull it to the mother's mouth; then put one or two fingers in, and pull strongly; and if the mother's mouth is constricted because of a hot swelling that has come there, then you should not strain, but rather administer moist and greasy things; and the administrator applies plasters, and uses warm softening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the child is on his side, and you can set him straight, then treat it as we have said for the living child; and if you cannot, then draw out the arrow piece by piece, leaving nothing of the fletching behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done this, treat it as we have said for abscesses that come into the flesh; and if there is a flow of blood, put it in warm water to stop the bleeding, and give other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	 And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had died, then another was born above that one, and the other also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	 After a long time she developed an abscess in her womb, which swelled so much that it burst open and began to fester greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	 I was called to tend to it, and thought about it for a long time, yet the wound could not be healed.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	 I placed on it a strong plaster, and from it came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	 I was greatly amazed by this, for the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	 So I thought that it must be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I probed the wound, and took out many bones, until the woman was in better condition; and she lived for a long time thus, and it often oozed a little from the place; and I have remembered this chapter only because, when a master finds something strange, he should know how to apply help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	 to return the bone to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	 Hereafter comes the form of the press, to which one attaches the weights; and at two turns are the two eyes of the two levers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the restrainer, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood should be two thumbs wide, and the margin of the trees one thumb, and in length a palm and a half; and between the two levers there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are fastened to each other at both ends, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are pushed into the mouth of the bone to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, more subtle and lighter, made from ebony wood or boxwood, resembling pincers; it should have at the two ends two adjustments, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the vulva with the entire instrument, let the woman sit on a bed, her feet dangling and her legs spread apart, then push the two adjustments together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs; then work your hand over the entire instrument, as you have done with the pincers equally, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the vulva, until the bailiff does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	 This instrument are all assembled, and their appearances are varied; and when the physician has prepared them, the work is more urgent, and higher for men due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	 Do not despair of the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze gently, and keep your hands over her mouth and nose; if she faints from this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cinnamon and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in water over the fire. Then put a reed or tube from the pot into the mouth of the woman, and hold it until the vapor enters inside her. Then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	 If the ligament is quickly torn.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment, and is not very strong, then instruct the nurse to moisten her left hand in olive oil or muslin with althea, and then insert it into the vagina, and seek for the ligament; and when she has found it, then take hold of it and stretch it little by little straightly, so that the uterus does not prolapse at the extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; and it will come out and relax.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the uterus is narrowly constricted, we have said the treatment for sneezing, and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not do so from all that we have said, then be careful not to be foolish in pulling; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the uterus, you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then give her an enema with tetrafarmacon oil; and it will soften and return, and come strong; but nevertheless, when it softens, a bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and it hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	 If it is necessary, therefore, suitable fumigations for this are as follows: some of the ancients have proven fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	 The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for retention of the menses and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 It is made of glass, similar to a reed, and the fine end is inserted into the vagina, while the wide end is placed over the fire; and let the fumigation be on charcoal, and continue until it has been thoroughly smoked out, and then begin again with another.
de percier lou fondement	 to pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born with their anus not yet pierced, but rather closed by a thin membrane: it is therefore necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her finger, and she should not pierce it with a sharp point, and be careful that she does not touch the linen with her hand; then place on moistened linen in wine and oil, then continue with ointment treatment until it is healed.  ?>
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	 And if you doubt that it will not heal, place a lead tube in the opening, and leave it for a few days, and remove it when the child wants to go into the rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	 And sometimes this blockage comes from the sudden closing of a wound or an abscess; then you must cover that sudden closure: and it should be treated as we have said with the lead tube.
de la fistule dou fondement	 of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodular, and those that come near the anus or in the space of the two parts, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this nodulation is old, it works, and also produces more moisture, either white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by the fact that something comes out in the evacuation or flatulence when the patient has an evacuation, and perhaps one of them bursts.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	 And so with fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and halfway through the penis; and they reach as far as the hip joint, and to the end of the heel.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one knows the fistula penetrating into the anus, and not penetrating: it is that you insert your finger in the anus, and thrust a subtle needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twist.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is twistiness, then thrust a subtle leaden tent or horsehair into it, until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and nothing comes out of the hole except wind or dung, as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; then hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	 And when the fistula extends to the bladder or to the passage of urine, then the urine leaks out, and it cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated to the junction of the thigh, then the swelling comes to that place; if there is no twist and the pain surrounds the area, then it leaks out constantly, and neither medicine nor salve by ointment helps; and in these penetrating fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of foolish physicians who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In the one that is not penetrating and is not old, there is hope of health through iron, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he raises his legs up to his thighs, and let his thighs be inclined towards his belly; then insert a probe of iron, or of lead if there is a twist, so that you know where the probe comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your index finger, and if you then feel that the tent has been pierced; and if it is uncovered where you sense between your finger the sinus or flesh, then know that it is a fistula; in which case do not labor over it, for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 However, it can be said that some can be healed well, but this happens rarely; and the help that is done for them is that one heats a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and inserts it very hot into the fistula until it reaches near the anus; and does this two or three times, so that you know that those fleshy parts are burnt, which resemble a bird's feather; and then cures the wet tent with butter, until that flesh comes out, then cures the wound with ointment, grease, and suturing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If he is healed thus, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If not, he cannot be healed in any other way; and if the tent between the fingers does not penetrate to the bone that is at the base, and there is a thick covering of flesh or sinew between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula where the covering ends at the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward always, and afterwards cauterize until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be freed and fall; then clean away those fleshy parts that resemble a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	 And if the pus overcomes you and flows between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or strong medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 Car the fire cautery brings together two good things: namely, the burning of these hairs close to each other, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then cure of wet tents in butter or crushed substances, until the place swells, and thus the burned flesh remains in the swelling; then treat the wound with hardening ointments that dry out flesh, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	 When it is healed, it is healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	 And if the fistula reaches to the very bottom of the anus and is distant from the body, if you push your finger into the anus and search thus.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent, and there are two layers between it, either linen or silk or flesh, and it is about to perforate, there is no remedy other than by means of one of these three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut through to the bottom, or if you can, place tents and treat it as before; but do not go too deep, lest you cut the ligament that holds the anus, causing involuntary excretion; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or remove that covering and clean it after it is cut near the anus, either with a tent or with another appropriate instrument; then clean away the dead flesh in the wound as much as you can; then endeavor to restore the wound, and make the fistula remain in the part outside the anus: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas are like this: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side of the anus near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	 And put a twisted thread in it, and push the tent along with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is pus in the margin of the anus within, then extract the thread from that opening, so that you put your finger into the anus; and pull the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and press one against the other, and leave it for one day or two; and constrict sometimes, until the thread cuts these fleshy parts that are between the two, and drop; then treat the wound until it is healed and cured.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	 If the fistula does not burst, then make it burst in all ways that you can, unless it is too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it is not right to cover the wound so deeply for healing, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The form of the spatula-shaped needle used for making the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side it is not, so that you do not cut what you should not cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	 hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and blood flows from them; and there may be one or several, and they are outside the anus and at the edge of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes a little citrine water or a little blood comes out, and they have the color of the body; and the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is that you instruct the patient to wash so as to go into the room, until the anus protrudes from him, and the threads appear; then hurry, and hold it with tongs, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut its roots; and if the fingers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with a small cloth, or with cotton, or with a piece of linen; and stretch them between your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle some hot powders on top that are suitable for cauterization; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, then treat with other treatments until healed; and if the anus cannot protrude, then give the patient a harsh and bitter enema to clean what is in the anus so that it can come out openly; when the patient sits down, and the threads come out of the anus, the treatment is light; and it is that you take them with your fingernail or with tongs, and cut them, then treat them as we have said until healed, and let him fear the iron incision.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If you must sew according to this method: take a thread, put it through a needle, then pull the thread out and make the needle go through from the other side; turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and make it wide; tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving one for draining excess blood; then place a piece of cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate on the wound, and tell the patient to rest; and leave it until it heals, and when they have healed, treat them with ointment and other treatments until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	 of dryness from the bottom
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	 Often there is dryness in the intestines due to natural constraint, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then you must scrape off the skin with a spatula or your fingernail, so that it does not moisten; then treat it until it is dry as it should be; and if it cannot dry out, then start scraping again more strongly than before, until it bleeds a lot and is scraped away; then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	 from shivering
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Ants are a small insect that lives under the skin and goes very deep; sometimes it feels cold, and one experiences it like death from shivering, and it affects the whole body, but more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is such that you take a quill of a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place this quill on the trembling, until the circle encompasses the entire trembling; then turn your hand to all the quill so that you strike around the entire trembling, and insert it deeply, and uproot the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	 And if you see this, do so with a quill of iron or steel according to this form, and let it be subtle below and drawn above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	 nor should it be perceived, to move and hold the two, and press more And if you see this, then cauterize the trembling, as it is written in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	 About the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	 Any time one makes an enema of silver or copper, or of melted bronze or iron; and sometimes these instruments are made in small and large sizes, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	 Therefore, those intended for the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	 The form of the small and large enema is thus wide at the top, where the stomach is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And there should be an opening where the stomach is tied, as you see, and the head should be perforated inside; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other one; and the stomach where one puts the medicines should be made from a bladder of an animal or parchment, and it should be perforated all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be one finger's width, then insert into these holes a strong thread of twisted wool in the shape of X or O, and assemble the stomach like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then give an enema; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, and the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold,
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you give him an enema in case of diarrhea, and the medicine rushes out, then restart it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are hemorrhoids or abscesses in the anus, then let the enema be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema where the skin should be pulled taut:
des plaies	 wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 We have already spoken in the section on the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines, according to their preparation.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere,
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care whether it is from the fall of a stone or similar things, and if the skin is nevertheless torn and the wound is large, and you doubt a hot abscess: then make it bleed immediately with cephalic vein blood, even if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite to the injured part; and advise the patient against overindulgence in wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be reduced, and do not let him drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if there are hot abscesses, only cotton soaked in rose oil or stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, put on the fresh wound with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if the heat has moved it, put on some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together with sutures, as I will say for the wounds of the belly, with suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.
