This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often happens to cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and it goes throughout the body rising and falling, and one feels it well when moving from limb to limb until it reaches the skin where it goes, and it jumps out; and it is engendered by the corruption of some humors, just as worms and snakes and leeches and ascaris in the belly; and one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being healed and drawn out, one cannot do more than when it goes: therefore, it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong ligature very tightly, then cut above and draw strongly, and if the pus has entered deeply into the flesh, and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head of the eye, hold the sorcil firmly below it, then cut above, and draw strongly; and one must use the patient for body cleansing with dissolving medicines for bad humors that cause putrefaction, and feed on foods that prevent putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and can move from one member to another; and I have seen those whom I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to an ailing woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise up like a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, as if quicksilver when it runs from place to place; the pain left that spot and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a short time later it ran throughout the body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it was turning around her body continuously, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 I marveled greatly at how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never before seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 However, I had seen many who had experienced pain moving from one place to another, but I had never seen it as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins were uncovered, and for this reason those constrained windinesses appeared; and it did not appear according to this reasoning with those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see this illness being cured and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then immediately bind above and below, and then cut open until that constrained windiness comes out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then cure it with those who dispel windinesses, such as stinking pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	 Arrows vary according to their types and the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The diversity of their types is such that there are those with large points and small ones, barbed and solid; and those with two edges, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that strikes a member does so in two manners: it lodges in a principal member, as in the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it strikes one of these members and the signs of death that I will tell you about later appear: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death follows in many cases; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not deeply lodged, then draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the signs of the skull when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and jumps the bone fragment that is on the skull, are faintness, dizziness, fainting, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of mind, vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is flow from the nose, or from the ears; and perhaps he loses his speech and voice; and from the wound moist white matter like brain, and also as a trickle of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then hold yourself ready for the cure, and draw out the arrow if it is there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like a finger, and black blood flows from it, and coldness and cold sweat come on, and syncope: know then without doubt that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	 And the sign of an arrow that never leaves the wound is without foamy blood spurting from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And if the arrow falls into the cover of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great heaviness and breathing difficulty; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	 And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested flesh will spurt from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	 And if the arrow falls into the belly, and some fecal matter spurts from the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 And if an arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine spurts out and flows away, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	 The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and chest and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	 When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you that happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to me once that an arrow fell on the bridge of my nose at its root; I pulled it out, and pushed it through from the other side under the fat of the ear, and healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And he shot an arrow from a bow that struck him in the fat of the eye under the eyebrow below, and the arrow was stuck, and he could not reach anything but the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large, like a Turkish bow, with all its iron light without ears; the wound was healthy, and no evil incident befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And he shot an arrow from the throat at a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I shaved the beard, and refined until I shot it, and the Christian was healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And he shot an arrow at a man, which had fallen into his stomach, and I thought he would die; but after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his disposition; I cut over the arrow, and fastened it, and shot it strongly, and he had no evil incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you see a man in whom an arrow fell into the back, and the wound was closed over it; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And if you see another man, in whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was closed; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And pulled an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had fallen into his nose, and was inclined slightly to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to the care after it fell for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 Si j'avoie a traitre le sang en luy?
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 Et je trouvai la plaie si estreinte que elle avoit peu d'entrée pour l'air venir dedenz.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 Quant je viz l'emplaistre, il fu si bien ajustez que ele tenoit moult fermement sur la plaie, et ele ne se remuoit point.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 Et quant je le vi, ele fu si bien ajustez que ele tenoit moult fermement sur la plaie, et ele ne se remuoit point.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 Et quant ele fu overte, la tentai et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the doctors judged that the nasal cartilage could not be restored; yet I restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was made whole.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 And I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you may apply your cure to those which I do not speak of, for the book cannot include everything; but the wise master compares well from a small thing, and from what is present and defective, he finds new work and new instruments in the practice of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows should not be removed from the members in which they are fixed except in two ways: either through the place where they entered or from another side; and those which go out through the place where they entered are arrows entering into fleshy places, and such sometimes nowadays.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not come out now, then leave it until the flesh is rotten around it, and the opening is clear; and likewise if it is lodged in the bone, and cannot come out, then leave it for some days and move it each day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, then pierce all around with a very fine needle, until the area around is enlarged, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, or any of the accidents that I have mentioned happen to the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it until it has equalized after some days, because if the arrow reaches the brain, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not lodged deep into the bone only, and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains for some days without bad incident, then use the method of drawing out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it is deeply lodged in this way and cannot come out, then apply dressings around it, as I have told you; then heal the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is hidden in the body such that it cannot be seen, then search all over for it; and if you feel it, then draw it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then widen the wound until it is large enough; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has barbs that catch on the flesh, then cut away the flesh that is lodged in two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow until you can draw it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you would draw it out more severely.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	 And if you cannot do it all at once, leave it until the place around it is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is contrary to you, then administer as we have said in the chapter on healing; and beware of cutting the nerve or vein, and devise a way how you can safely draw out the arrow quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help there can be. And if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another place, or if it brings something out of itself, or the skin is swollen in such a way that one can see or feel it clearly: then cut on top of it, so that the pincers can take hold, and then pull it out: if it is stuck now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	 And if it is lodged in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, then leave it still and begin the extraction again until it comes out with force; and if the arrow's shaft is there, push all of the shaft; and if the shaft has fallen off, and you see that pushing is being done, then administer a falling instrument, so that the point of the arrow enters the gap of the instrument; and then push with force, and if the arrow has been pushed out, then insert an entering-point instrument to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls in the pelvis or in the stomach or in the bladder or in the ribs, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut above it, then cut; and be careful not to cut the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound if necessary; and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	 The shape of the tongs used to remove arrows resembles a bird's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 And there are many types of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the end of the probe is like the feather of a bird, to push at the tip of the arrow, as shown in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	 The form of tongs for pushing and pulling is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	 of the common body's veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The veins from which one bleeds are XXXI, of which there are XVI in the head, namely: II large ones that are behind the ears, called the two "herbech"; and II arteries that are in II temples; and II veins that are in II eyelids, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the II tendons that are in the neck; and the II veins that are on the upper lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and II veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, which is located on the left side, and common people call it "vein of the head"; and the median vein is called "faste", which is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is located on the right side, and common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the ulnar vein, and this is the one that is commonly used for bleeding, which appears clearly on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the salvatelle vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the wrist of the left side, and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is on the other ankle; and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The bleeding of wounds that are after the ears aids in ancient catarrhs, and in migraines; and the qualities of the bleeder, as I tell you, is to lift up the head of the patient, and rub the place where the wounds are with a rough cloth; then have the patient constrict his neck with a screw, until the two wounds appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head: squeeze them then with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse beneath your thumb, hold it there; then take the lancet, and push it under the wound to the bone, then lift up your hand all along the wound, and cut both the skin and the wound very well two fingers wide across, and let out as much blood as you wish; then constrict and bind, until it is healed; and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for an old migraine, and headache, and customary eye inflammation; and the qualities of the bloodletting are as I say: and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly; and he feels the pulse beneath your finger, then signifies with a nod; then raise the chest above the vein high to your finger's indication, and insert the lancet below, and lift the vein high, and cut it as you have done in two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your necessity; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; and then bandage it well, and leave it until it heals; and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The bleeding from the vein of the forehead is as valuable as the bleeding from the cephalic in ancient facial diseases, and for migraine, and for rougeur; and the quality is such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur," of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the point on the vein, and strike with your hand or something else, and let blood come out according to the quantity you wish; then release the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is healed, and sometimes work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 However, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp; and to bleed diagonally, because the bone is close, and by chance it breaks the subtle flame.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 And if the flame is subtle, by chance it may break; then make flow of the blood, as much as you need, and then bind on a cushion, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The bleeding from the vein of the nose is good for gout and madness and diseases of the face, such as migraine and rougeur that comes to the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of the blood is such that the patient strains his neck, then presses his nose against your left hand, and take a subtle, long flame, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deeply, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, for it is very quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The bloodletting of the two veins helps with the narrowing of the temples, and with the onset of madness, and with many diseases, and with impetigo, and with erysipelas, and with herpes and styes; and the nature of the bloodletting is such that the patient holds his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein for a while widely, then draw the temperate blood, as much as needed; then repeat the same in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and hold both veins moderately, so that the patient does not constrict; and leave it until morning, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the bleeding of livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	 The bleeding of wounds of the lips above helps in healing within the mouth, and against corruption of the gums, and cracking of the lips, and of the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the quality of the bleeding is to make the patient sit before you and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the two wounds, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by their being black, and because around them there are small black veins: therefore cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them and you are in doubt, then cut the largest from each part, and also do the same with the two wounds that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the wound under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The wound of the wounds that are under the tongue thus helps after the wound of the cephalic, and this is for the constriction of the throat, and for the diseases of the eye, and for the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the wounder are such that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and looks under on each side a black wound: thus bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep, because below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The wounds of the knife with which one commonly bleeds are bled in two manners: either by pricking with all one flame-shaped broad, or olive-like subtle as sharp knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are broad and subtle according to the breadth and narrowness of the wounds.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	 The shape of the Martin flame is very renowned, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary for opening veins full of thick, visible blood, which contain thick and turbid blood; this is the shape of the olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	 It is more subtle and pointed, for healing subtle veins, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids in diseases that are under the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the stomach; and it is necessary for the healer to heal wisely, and to beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if he cuts the artery, and blood begins to flow, it must be stopped, as I have said; and the flame should not be pinching, but cutting like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilic does not open clearly, then you must restrain it and choose another one; or you may seek some remedy from it, or heal in its place the vein in the middle of the arm: it opens clearly; and cut with the lancet flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you see the place of the vein, then you must immediately restrain the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place above it, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the lancet flame; and beware that you do not strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for that is of the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it coming out like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from an artery: hurry then, and place your finger on top for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; if it does not stop, bind the arm, and leave it like this, and let the patient not move it; and let him be afraid, and do not move it until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	 And if the bleeding is not stopped, and it weakens you, and a doctor is not present, cut the artery if it is open, for the head of the vessel will retract; and stop the blood flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And take a strip of linen and split it in half, and take one of the halves and tie it well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then heal it as we have said, with powders that stop blood flow; and the stoppage is not very difficult in many situations due to the smallness of the wound and the strength of the arm's bandage.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The wound in the middle thus helps that it draws blood from above and below the head, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the healer to be cautious of the nerve that is beneath, and if he pierces too deeply into the depths, and finds the nerve, and it swells and the patient may be displeased, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens very often, and if it does not open in some men due to its subtlety, then you must bleed him with an instrument called anesil; and avoid the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	 And if there is a wound between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The saining of the cephalic vein aids in drawing blood from the head and helps the eyes; one must sang in a pointed manner towards the olive tree or the mirtle leaf, for it is the safest of all veins, because under it there is neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest place, and it is not serious if one misses the first time, and one tries again; and sometimes the site swells in some men when one misses the first time, but it is not serious.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the bleeding depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you must know about bleeding is that bleeding is only administered to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins, which are: cephalic, fast and basilica; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring in the fall and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no set time, but rather when needed by day or night, at all hours and at all times; and it is not appropriate to bleed children until the age of fourteen, nor a woman carrying a child from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 Nor should the old who have passed sixty years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, he must first empty the intestines with a light enema if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the harmful superfluities to the main members; nor should one bleed who is too full of food, or drunk until sober, or suffering from dropsy; and one must refrain from bleeding after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, increased frequency of intercourse with a woman, travel, vigil, fasting, and everything that weakens the whole body, whether by weapon wound or bodily injury; then subtilize the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicines, if you have the power to do so; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein of the foot around the third hour, as we have said; and guard that day against labor, pain, lust, and similar things; and be joyful and happy, and let the person bleeding you be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature moderately, for if it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the place with the hands until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the person bleeding you with a little old oil, then place his left hand's finger on that vein below the place where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not flee or fail at the time of incision.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 Car il y a des veines qui fuient comme des cordes au sainier, et il y en a d'autres qui sont pleines de ventosité, donc quand on met le feu dessus, elles reculent du feu et ne peuvent ouvrir la veine, ainsi est-on avec celles-ci; et si on ouvre la veine, alors la plaie est trop étroite, pour cela il faut que le saigneur soit averti de ces choses.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 And if the vein is opened the first time, that's good; but if not, then begin again a little below that place or quickly above, unless the place is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the place is swollen and the patient is alarmed, leave it for one or two days and do not tie up the arm: perhaps such abscesses will form; do not enter into a bath, then resume the bloodletting if he wishes; and if the opening is small or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that enough blood will come out as you wish, then pour all of the fire directly into that same opening; and work a little quickly, before the place swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the area swollen, do not begin to cauterize again, and apply a little oil of lily, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the ointment is called the oil of lilies; and thus administer the ointment of oil in each cautery that you cauterize the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same action makes a plaster and a poultice from them, when placed on the area; it subtilizes the blood and disperses when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not cauterized strongly enough that only this time and the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and place on the area a moistened sponge in water and salt, warm, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains on the area after several days, it does not harm; and if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh soaked in calamus juice, mastic, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 And many times there occurs an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica: therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the touch of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore avoid putting any of the things we have mentioned on it, for perhaps there is a leak from an artery; but make an I dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw out from each person's blood according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see that it is thick, let it flow until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And he who is strong and robust, if he needs bloodletting, one should make a larger wound for him, and the flame should be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and one must often bleed him little by little, and one should bleed him in cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive blood loss and nerve damage, and it is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And for him whose body is deficient in bleeding, one should give moistened bread in apple juice; if he is heated, then draw blood three or four times. And if he has a cold temperament, let him chew before the bleeding moistened bread in muscadine syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he bleeds profusely after losing much blood, then he should drink broth of meat and subtle scented syrup, and use the other things that we have mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope, to evacuate the veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wishes to bleed from his arm and to bleed again at another time, then it is necessary that when he is weakened by great bleeding, he should bleed a little at a time, according to the amount of his strength, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	 And if he wishes to bleed from his arm after the first bleeding, and he is strong-bodied, then let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And whoever wants to heal from elsewhere, he must heal on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 Because there is much blood within the body that is already heated and causes fever; therefore, one must draw out a great quantity of it and widen the opening until it flows in a steady stream; then you should consider all the conditions for healing, and place your hand on the pulsating vein when it heals, so that death does not come in the place of the wound, and this happens often when the healer is negligent; and it is not necessary, when you want to release the arm, and make the blood come out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press very hard; nor if it is curved, should he extend his arm quickly, for that would be bad; but leave it until it heals a second time; or you place at the tip of the flame, so that the frozen blood at the opening of the wound comes out, and put on a little silk bag filled with water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	 And if there is a need to bleed for the second time, then heal it in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	 The veins inside the arm are healed in the place of the head vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of healing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the fingertips turn red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears well, and heal it now by traversing, not wide or long; and let the opening be large, and heal it very close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is used more in winter than in summer; and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, because there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The wound of the little finger on the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is how it should be done: stretch out the hand, and place it in hot water until the vein swells up, if you see it; and if the wound turns sideways, or if you cut it all the way through, it does not matter; but do not go too deep, for the nerves are bare under all the skin, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, then place oil and salt on the vein to seal it quickly, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	 The bleeding from his left hand is worth as much as the disease of the mouse, and does just as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The bleeding from the spleen is worth as much against all the diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of his bleeding is such that the patient should put their foot in hot water, and rub on the vein until it bursts, and tie above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins; then bleed where the largest vein is, or at the ankle, for that is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And if you heal on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and cut across as in slicing; and let the flame be swift.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot back in water, and let the wound drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the healer makes a mistake the first time, then start again the second time a little higher, for the place is salty; do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the saphena of the other foot likewise.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	 The place of the sciatic wound is at the ankle on the back, and its healing is worth the pain in the hip, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, and the nature of his bleeding is such that the patient enters the bath, and draws four thumbs above the ankle in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then bleed him in all the manners that you can, and by crossing; and it is better that you cut it, for the place is hollow, and it is very responsive to many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you do not find it, then bleed some vein of him that opens on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let as much blood flow as you wish, and then unbind the ligature, and place cotton and compress it; she is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	 Of the cupping glasses
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 Cupping glasses are made of horn, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking to draw blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cupping which is without striking is done in two ways: either at full heat or without heat; and the cupping that is done by striking and extracting blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is entirely on top of the head; and another is in the neck; and two others on both sides of the neck; and the cups below the chin; and the cups on both shoulders; and the cups on the hips; and the cups on both arms; and the cups on both legs; and the cups on both ankles; and this cupping does not draw blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken anyone at all, as one does with venesection; and it should not be administered, neither with full heat nor without heat, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.  ?> And this cupping which is done without striking is in two ways: either with full heat or without heat; and the cupping which is done by striking and extracting blood is done in fourteen places on the body: one entirely on top of the head, another in the neck, two others on both sides of the neck, the cups below the chin, the cups on both shoulders, the cups on the hips, the cups on both arms, the cups on both legs, and the cups on both ankles. This cupping does not draw blood except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken anyone at all, as one does with venesection; and it should not be administered, neither with full heat nor without heat, in any disease that comes from repletion until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if because of necessity or disease one must use cupping therapy, either by habit or custom, we administer it every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and at all times; for there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and there are those who find swelling and redness on their face, and on their head, and on the neck, and darkness in the eyes; and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are those who dream, and see nothing but blood and wounded and dead people and such things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order cupping after every three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief …
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	 Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The cauterization at the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, migraines, and strangulation, as well as toothache at the roots, and it is in the place of the sinus of the basilica; and it is necessary that you instruct the patient not to cut the artery when applying.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 The cauterization under the chin is good for mouth diseases, and for rotting of the gums, and similar diseases in the mouth; and it is in the place of the sinuses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 The cauterization of the shoulders is good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The cauterization of the ribs is as effective as that of the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to strike too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and lies under nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	 The cupping glass that is on the rump serves for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases below, and it must be large, and made of brass, so that it can draw well; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 The cupping glasses of the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and they are good for old pains of the kidneys, and of the spleen, and of the bladder, and they remove flows; and they are placed on the II saphenous veins, and on the II ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring fever in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	 The way to apply the cupping glass is that you first place it empty, and suck immediately, and put it on quickly, and move evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then strike, and replace the cupping glasses, and pay attention to the arrangement of the body, for there are such people who have dark flesh and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and deep enough; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 And if the flesh is thick, you must strike twice: the first time to open the way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And if the flesh is very thick, you must strike a third time; and when we want to draw out a little blood at a time, we only need to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want to draw much blood, then we bleed often; and if the blood is thick, then strike deeply, and the end of it is that the heart should be suddenly pierced; and those who have thick skin and hard, and whose pores are narrow, you must anoint the places of the cupping glasses with oil that opens and dissolves: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	 And if the superfluidities are thick and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the person being healed has tender flesh and large pores, one should not put oil there, but it should be washed after evacuating with rose water, or cold water, or mallow water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar waters.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And those who have much moisture should be lifted with easel, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have excessive superfluidities should be lifted with old wine, or water of fig, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar things; and one must not heal with cupping before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that they wash themselves, when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 Et warder if the patient is coleric and if his blood is too hot and inflamed; then he should take cold things such as quinces and endives and lettuce in vinegar, and similar things; and eat less, and chicken meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And those with cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and medium-aged aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and less meat, and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he will bleed himself, he must drink more than eat; and some men should be given triacle or muscate before or after bleeding to strengthen the main members; and the blood should be thinned, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink it.
