Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos mettons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	 The form of the cupping glass applied to fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 It should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and it should have on the side around the middle a small hole, just large enough to insert a needle, and let it be of brass, smooth on the inside so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there should be a rod of brass or iron across for placing a candlewick, and both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the cupping glasses for children are different from those for the elderly, and for the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one must place this cupping glass on the limb in this way: take the candlewick of wax or linen, and place it inside the cupping glass across the rod that is inside the cupping glass, so that the light is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and let your two fingers be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when you want, out goes the vapor, and remove the cupping glass; and take the candlewick as before, and repeat it often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the application of the cupping glass in the disease of pleurisy, there is no rod or hole, and it is only prepared when it is full of water, and it is placed on the member alone; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Without being prepared for members where one cannot place cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places without flesh, such as fingers or noses, and other similar ones; and the quality of use is that when you find leeches that are in clean waters without contamination, take them; and put one nut in clean water, until they become familiar with it, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let them be drawn from vein and cupping glass, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the leeches on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where one can place a cupping glass, put one on, because this is very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, then lift the place of ease, and then with water, very well, and then press it; and if the place is too healthy after the leeches, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it there until the bloodletting is exhausted; and if the bloodletting is multiplied, then place on vitriol powder, or gallnuts, and similar things, until it is exhausted; or you place on the place half of peeled beans, and leave them until they dry on the place, it will now staunch; and if you need more, then take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the leeches do not want to attach, then rub the place with fresh blood, or you insert a needle until the blood comes out, and then place them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are full, then sprinkle on a pouch of powdered aloe and henbane, or ashes, and they will now fall off.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	 Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	 This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the treatment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that the foolish doctors cast aside this chapter, as they have never seen any ancient books or read any letters about it; and for this reason, knowledge is lost in our land, for I have never found any good ones; and I know nothing except by the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have acquired the knowledge, and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have already described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	 It is therefore necessary that we speak in the prologue of this book about the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or breaking happens to someone, you must hasten to heal the patient on both sides, unless something prevents you completely, such as physical weakness, infancy, old age; or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and avoid cold food, that is to say cold baths, and bird meat and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess or spreading matter in the limb; then the patient should return to his first governing diet.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	 And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with foods that provide abundant nourishment and viscosity, such as boiled wheat in water, and rice, and heads (of animals), and feet, and cow's udder, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	 For with such nourishment the bones heal and do so more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or mend according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of young children; but there is no concern, reset above the broken bone thick tenons which tighten and join the limb together, until it regains its previous strength; and if not completely, then at least partially, for this reason the patient must be nourished with abundant foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	 And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	 For the fracture of the head is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	 For there is a fracture that goes to the shin, and another by sharpening, like the point of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	 And there is also fracture with wound, and fracture where there is a small crack throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each kind has its own device and proper instrument for restoration, according to how the memory returns to its place; and it is known that the fracture of the bone because the place is twisted, and it appears well from afar, and sounds on pressing with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but it may well have twisting, or cracking, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	 Si it is not necessary for you to move it with your hand, but apply the following remedies, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that if the break goes into the air and the two parts are disjointed, you must now set them equally point by point before an abscess comes; and if an abscess comes, leave it for a day until the abscess is appeased; then set it in place as you can lightly and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of one with pieces; then restrain it as required hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if in the bone there are pieces broken, and they are divided into two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or at your hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the limb are freed, you reset by all means the additions in their places as you can, and be careful not to cause injury or pain to the patient through your work; and join well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 And you can tell it is not right with the hand if it seems to you that it is not: so make it beautiful and do not hold it too tightly, nor press as those who bring about hot abscess and contracture in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient well that he not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when he feels any pain, it is not in place, and it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain; and ensure that it is set straight, lest crookedness come to it when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	 Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness, largeness, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones: wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and thighs: wrap them with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandage embraces all of the large limb, and holds it evenly on all sides, so that there is no gap; then bind light wool around it, three or four turns according to the limb, and hold your hand a little taut against all the bandages, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break moves slightly away from the break; and soften the bandage a little at a time, until you take a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage, and turn it again around the broken place; then go back to the part below the break, and hold it moderately, not too tight or too loose, as we have said in the first turn above; then put linen wool or cloths between the bandages, so that they are all even, then bind everything on top with one bandage, and then place your splints well made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or abscess, apply something that soothes the abscess and removes the swelling, and leave it thus for some days; then press on your supports, and let them be made of half the width of a reed, or of wood from which clives are made, or of palm branches, according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But the support that one puts on the fracture must be a little thicker and wider than the others; and it should be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether small or large; then press on the supports as you did in the first layer, then tie above with thread, as in the first layer over the break; tighter at first, then less so; and the threads must be medium, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen the work of fools who make their ties from twisted linens, and that is a great error, for the tie cannot be equal if it is too tight, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each support.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	 And if the patient is wounded by the heads of the bones after setting them in their places, place under them linen rags or shreds of wool, so that he does not become wounded.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	 When the wound is with a fracture, and the heart is broken, I will speak of its treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	 And know that it is not fitting to reset all the broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 Because when the member is large, it is not fitting to place bones until after five days or seven, or more according to your skill in dealing with abscesses; and see here the manner of old emplasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and sprain: and it is that you take flour that stays at the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of eggs, and place this confection, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common manner of the emplaster restoring fractures in many dispositions, and especially for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 Another manner of plaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twisting: take 3 ounces of pepper, laudanum, enula, asafoetida, gum arabic, and mastic, 10 ounces; myrrh and aloes, 5 ounces; garlic 9 ounces; and make it into powder, and mix with the white of an egg; if a man's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another plaster for twisting: take mastic and marshmallow, 10 ounces; myrrh and aloes, 9 ounces; acacia, 6 ounces; Armenian bole, 10 ounces, and grind well, and make into a poultice with the white of an egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, and la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, and met sus lou leu.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, but it is good for alleviating hot abscesses and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Another way to make a plaster that mends broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth pear leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to make a plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to absorb any remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take the root of mullein, chamomile, violet flowers, chickpea flour, one part each; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of plaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of mullein, flax seeds, balsam, melilot, and sansevieria, and violet and chamomile flowers, equal parts of each; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	 Ypocras says in his book that one should not raise the broken limb to restore its strength, but rather use a salve made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	 And it seems to Galen that one should raise the broken limb to restore it with dry and slightly warm things such as myrrh, aloes, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Another way to make a plaster that helps with injury and pain: take mugwort, clipped horse tails or bird feathers, marshmallow, and celery, grind them up, and make a plaster out of it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	 And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, I have removed everything from it, and you need to use a plaster and bandage, then begin again as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if nothing comes to the member as we have said, then do not unbind it before III days or IV or V or VII; and sometimes leave it XX days, according to what is seen, until the fracture hardens, and the setting of the flesh approaches; then restrain it more than at first, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see the place drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; therefore, moisten it with warm water, every time you unbind it, which should be every III days, and release the bandage a little; by this work thus the nourishment comes to the member, and quickly mends what foolish doctors do wrongly: they twist the member badly: this is bad, and such work is fearful, and I see nothing there but to leave it and work on it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	 Of the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 There are many ways of breaking and diverse forms, and the causes are distinct; for there are breaks caused by the blow of a sword, and the blow removes all the bone up to the marrow which is beneath the bone, just as an axe or stick does; and therefore this manner of break is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 Or if the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, this manner of break is called "absolue"; and the wound in these two breaks is either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	 And if there is an embedded strike, or a splintering or blow from a stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	 And if there is a persistent fracture, which reaches to the flesh beneath the bone, or is on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that penetrates into the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone or by falling or by any similar thing, and causes a piece of bone to enter below, and the place is split like blacksmiths do when they hammer on anvils; then the stone enters.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more often in those whose bones are moist at the top, like a child's head; and it occurs with all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated from them like stars; and I will speak about this later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	 Et reconnaissons toutes les sortes de fractures par leur déplacement, et par l'enquête sur les tendons, et par la chair corrompue qui se trouve dessus.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	 The hair-like appearance is known by this: when the bone is exposed and rubbed upon, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	 In the care of the fracture, beware of the patient's accidents, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, swooning, fever, and eyes coming out and turning red, and other similar things in many dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	 And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	 And when the wounded comes to you first, in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	 And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the cloth beneath the bone become corrupt, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the bone fracture reaches up to the cloth covering the brain, then you must split the affected part thus: and it is that you take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover above the bone in every way possible, and on the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or an abscess like this, if he helps with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and you are sure of the absence of bleeding; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two methods: one method is that you cut with a narrow incision from the front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	 And then he makes another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 And the second method is such that you have various cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed and made of Indian iron; and work lightly, so that you do not harm the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 And if the bone is protruding and hard, then you must bore around it before making cuts with trepanations, not too deep so as not to perforate the skull. The point should have a margin or ring above it so that the point does not pass through the bone; and you should have several of these, so that each one comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have trepanations for all skulls; and this is the form of the three types of trepanations:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 The quality for perforating around the broken bone is that you put the auger on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then remove the auger and place it elsewhere a little after, and do this all around, then cut with the scissors the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly and lightly than you can, as we have said, so that you draw the bone into your hand, or one of the instruments you have such as tongs, pincers; and beware not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced and drawn out the bone, it is necessary that you clean the residue that remains of the bone with all other similar instruments like scissors, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other scissors; and if there remain any small bones or scales, then remove them lightly with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and onions as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is safer; and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	 It is first necessary that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture opens, so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place under the head of this lancet-like instrument.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut from one side only, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly tap all around the bone, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath; if it is stuck to the bone, gently lift it up, for one can remove it without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	 And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through to the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then you must scrape off that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you should have various quantities, to administer in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	 Use first larger scrapers, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 In each of the other fine incisions and subtle fractures, it is necessary to administer treatment according to its nature; and this is something that is not easily answered by those who have studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the wound is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled cloth in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you do not burden the wound, then administer over it another bandage, and do not bind too tightly except to touch the wound only; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscess is appeased, then unbind it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place on the wound, and administer medicines that are not irritating; and be careful that the wound is always clean, so that you do not leave any grease, nor allow pus to collect, for when pus collects on the linen of the head, it will run and burst, and great harm will come to the patient; for when something irritating is placed on the wound, it hardens over it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	 Take heed then, if any misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness comes except for the medicine that has been applied, which has such power, it is necessary that you take a part of honey and III parts of rose oil and make a plaster with it; then apply it to the wound; then treat in various ways as needed until healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 Know that sometimes the two upper parts of the nose are broken, or only one by itself, for these are two bones; and the lower one is made of cartilage, and does not break, but only swells or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your little finger or a probe into the nose, and place that break evenly within your index finger, and push out through the nostril, until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	 And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach it, then you must place a large clump of hair evenly on top of a reed.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, then do the same, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when that swelling has subsided, then insert at the tip of the nose cloths of linen, if the break is in one part. 》
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 Where you push one bone into another part, if there is a fracture; and let the tendons be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some say that one should moisturize the tendons in butter, and change it daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem to me that this is good, but the tendons should be moistened in a mixture of egg white and powdered flour; then leave the tendon until the bone is healed, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 Sometimes goose feathers are inserted into the nose instead of tendons, and then a soft cloth is placed around it, and the fracture is held together, and the patient breathes through it; now do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	 And if boils like this come to the nose while you are working on it, then put a plaster or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a little bit of dysaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if boils like this do not come to the nose, then put a plaster on the outside, made of sesame flour and powdered incense, mixed with egg white, then place light dressings on top, and do not bind the nose; and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into tiny pieces, then use suitable instruments to realign it, then stitch the break, and treat with things that encourage flesh growth and healing, such as appropriate plasters and ointments for this purpose; and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat with tenths, and place lead weights until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	 of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	 When the jaw is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the break is only outside and not broken in two, unless it is splintered inside, then it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left jaw, then put your right index finger inside, and push the break lightly inside, and adjust it with the other hand from the outside, and make it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	 And if the jaw fracture is divided into two parts, then you must apply traction to both parts until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 And if there is movement of the teeth, or loosening, bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk; then place on the broken jaw poultice, and place on it a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large, well-made cushion, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it tightly at the chin as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then reset to the original position; and place a poultice on it, with flour from the mill mixed with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after removing the poultice; and place light linen on the poultice. And if the poultice becomes dry and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals; often it heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	 And if such abscesses occur, treat them as we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 And if there is both a fracture and a wound, check to see if any piece of the bone has been removed; then carefully remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	 And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, then close the wound if it is wide, and place on it suitable plasters to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	 of the splint
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 The splint breaks in several places towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and shattered into two pieces, and there are fragments, and this is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, that is when the fracture is without a wound, you should have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder which feels the force of the break; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then place the fracture equally between your fingers, so that the form be as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth or linen, and let it be thick according to your needs; and straighten and lift the broken part, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you may set the fracture equally as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	 And if you cannot pull the head of the broken part outward, because it comes in depth, then it is necessary that the patient lie on his back, and place under the shoulder a medium-sized pillow, and let the assistant push the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the break be raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 And then receive the fracture in your hands, and if you find it broken, you must cut through; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be rejoined due to any swelling, cut off one of the edges with an incisor that you have; but place under the forceps this instrument, to protect the soft tissue:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 and it should be like a spoon, and not made of iron, and it should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and it should have two heads, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, as is the contour of the wound that you have made when you have drawn out the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, sew up the wound, and if the contour is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, fill the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	 And if an abscess occurs there, soak the cloth in rose oil and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 And the straightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cuts, is that you place on the bone a poultice of milled powder and egg white, and put light wool on top, and put a sphere under the saddle if necessary; then take a very wide bandage of one palm in width, then put a double cloth over the wool, and the poultice; then take a thin strip of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging; and put the strip on the break, and turn the bandage up to the neck, and under the saddle of the patient; and tie each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the break well, and you see clearly that the strip does not move on the broken bone, then loosen it daily, and when the ligature loosens, tighten it again; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the saddle to raise the shoulder up; thus the break will lighten by the lightening of the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an adverse event occurs, for twenty days; then renew the poultice, if you see that he needs it, and tighten it and leave it so, until it is healed; and it is healed in a maximum of twenty-eight days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	 Of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 When the shoulder is broken in the large part or middle, and there is swelling except by touch; prepare it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the place powder from a mill with plenty of egg, and light stuffing, and put on double cloth; then put on a wide and thin board, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there are hollows under the board in any part of the shoulder, fill those hollows with linen stuffing, so that the board sits evenly; and then bind it all tightly with a large bandage, so that the board does not move from its place, and check the bandage every day; and each time it loosens, bind it again, and make the board equal if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 days or 25. And when this number is complete, then unbind him, and be sure, for this is not a bone that can easily move.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	 And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and points down towards the heart, it should be cut off, and do what we have said in the breaking of the rib to soothe the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	 of the foot's break
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the ankle.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it shifts downward, and the patient feels great pain, and loss of strength, and swelling, and sometimes vomits blood, and opens the passage in the broken bone, which can be felt well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the healing is that the patient lies frequently on their back, and one places a pillow between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and brings the ribs together from the second rib with your hands, and adjusts it to be equal in all ways that you can, until the bone shape is as it should be; then place bandages and wool over the thin board of salt or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it firmly on the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage smoothly around the back, and bind it tightly, and loosen it every hour, and if it softens, then tighten it; and if you need to loosen it, because of erosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and loosen it, and remove the bandage, and address whatever has come from ways of healing; then replace the bandage, and bind it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	 Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 Know that the fracture of the ribs comes only in large bones near the back and inside the head, and they only bend because they are cartilaginous; and one feels it well by examining two (ribs).
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the treatment is that you set the fracture straight, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 And then apply a poultice, and bind it with a bandage, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 And if the fracture of the ribs is inward, the patient feels very great pain and sharpness, as from pleurisy, for the bone points at the flesh; and he can hardly breathe, and soon vomits a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and the ancients have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	 And there are those who say that it should be administered food that swells the belly, to push out the breakage in excess.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	 We do not do this, for fear that hot abscesses may come to it, if they have not already done so.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	 And if they have come, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 And some say that one should put cupping glasses on the place to strongly draw out [the humors], and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping glasses may attract superfluous humors to the place due to the weakness of the patient's constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	 And some say that the place should be covered with oil-soaked wool, and tents are placed between the ribs to equalize the breath around it, then treat it with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear because of the bone that protrudes from the wound, and there is doubt for the patient, then one must incise over the broken rib, and place an instrument underneath to protect the lung; and then the bone should be cut, and gently drawn out, and then stitch the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if such an abscess occurs, place moistened cloths in rose oil on it, and put it on the spot; and treat the spot as one would for an abscess, and let it lie so until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	 of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and it can happen that it bends; and likewise with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is fatal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when pressed and pricked, know that the junction of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is injured or not, take care if the feet are numb, and if there are accidents in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and involuntary bowel movements; and when one has treated it on his belly, then there is involuntary bowel movement.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when he has been treated on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is fatal; do not bother with his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	 And if these symptoms do not occur, then the condition is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And the treatment is to check if there is a hot abscess, then apply rose oil or yolk of egg oil on the spine until it is soothed; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on that part where he feels the pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if any bone is exposed, it is necessary to cover on the skin; and remove the bone, then join the two lips of the wound with a stitch if it is large, then treat the wound with an ointment made from fat, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", if you put your little finger of your left hand in it, and make it equal to the other hand in power, then apply a compress and a bandage on top, if you need them; then bind it, and if there is bone exposure, then remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	 of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 If it happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, then there is only a little lessening at the top; and it breaks in length, and declines towards the outside, and it causes pain and bruising to the patient in that place, and swelling as if broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	 And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it until you are on top of the break; and know what kind of break and its form are; and if the break is only at the top, then align this break so that it is in natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	 And if the break is along the length, or it slants inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that you can prepare to restore this break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	 Et when you have made it equal, then put on the plaster, then put on a splint of wood or horn, and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and fill the place under the ribs, until the joint is level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	 And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	 And if an abscess occurs there, do not touch it until the abscess is healed, and put on what we have previously said; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as needed, unless there is no bad incident; and that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	 of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 The shoulder is that which is between the shoulder blade and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it should be restored in one of two ways: one of which is that you take a stake full of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 And tie at the two heads two cords, and pull them up, and make the patient sit on a seat; then cast the broken arm onto the stake, until it reaches the armpit, and has in the middle a bend of the stake; then pull up some heavy object where the attendant extends downward; then place the doctor the break equal to his hands together, so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	 And the other manner is that one makes the patient sit on his heels, and ties the hand to his neck; then commands two attendants that one holds that which is above the break in his hands, and the other holds below all together, and each extends at its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold tightly the tendon below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the members to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the fracture is near the shoulder's head, then you must place one ligament moderately below the armpit and another towards the back, under the fracture; similarly, if the fracture is towards the back, a light ligament should be placed without effort until the fracture is level on both sides; then set the fracture as needed, and hold it tightly, lest any abscesses form there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.
