And if such abscesses form there, do not hold it tightly for seven days, and place a wet cloth on it with oil rose, until the abscesses are soothed; then hold it tightly, and the manner of holding is such that you put the poultice on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; and apply the bandage, and hold both on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, unless anything prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints, and place on the fracture a wider and stronger splint than the others, and let there be two finger-widths between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends three finger-widths beyond the break on each side; then tighten the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less widely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the placement of the splints and the tightening as we have said, in the hour when you restore the broken limb, and you doubt a hot abscess, let it be bandaged until the seventh day, as we have said; then every three days check the bandage that itching or swelling does not come to the place, where nursing cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the patient accepts, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accident occurs, do not unbind it until after three days or more, and the patient should sleep on their back, with hands on their stomach; place one cushion filled with wool under the shoulder, and check every hour of the day or night that the appearance of the broken limb does not change, or that the ligament is not softened; accept it through the power of medicine, and give the patient the food that we have mentioned earlier, in such a way that the first course is subtle; and when they begin to recover, let the food be substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset within forty days in total; and then one must unbind them and administer a bath and remedies made from onions to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the constriction is ugly and swollen, it takes days or months to release.
de la brisure du bras	 of the arm fracture
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "foscile", one of which is small and follows the wrist; and the other is large and is located below, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large foscile breaks, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more serious than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small foscile that is broken, it should be slightly extended and made straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 Et si c'est le grand fémur, il faut alors le serrer plus fortement; et l'étendre sur un coussin, et tenir le pouce de la main plus haut que les autres doigts, et le petit doigt plus bas que les autres doigts, et que le malade soit croisé sur lui-même, et le coussin devant lui plus haut, afin que le malade ne ressente aucune douleur; puis étendre les ministres avec leurs bras à la partie en dessous de sa main, ou au lien, et un autre ministre à l'autre partie au-dessus.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the physician should place it evenly, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if it is broken into pieces, place each piece in its proper location; and if there is any that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut it out and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	 And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter; so take the treatment from there.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if at the beginning of the treatment abscesses like these occur, then take a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft; and bind the cloth on top skillfully, until those abscesses are relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the wax cloth, and apply a poultice of flour from the mill with plenty of egg, then place splints, and let the splint for the fracture always be stronger, and a little wider than the others; and know that there should be 6 splints on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones or in two; and bind more tightly over the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as it heals, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And return the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any evil accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must wash the limb with hot water until the itch is calmed; and let the limb not be constricted or rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the traction, and if the ligament is weakened and the bone separated, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And if one is careful that the nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too constricted, then you must soften it in the pouch and let it remain like this for some days until the nourishment comes, and then traction it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things that we have said happens to the patient, then do not unbind until 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 or around it, then let the patient grasp his hands around his neck, and let his neck be straight, and he should avoid movement and trembling, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in 30 days or 35, and perhaps even in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	 of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that on the back of the hand and around the fingers, there are few fractures, and it only happens that there is swelling many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And when the palm of the hand is broken or swollen, it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit straight in front of him equally; then place his hand on a flat surface, and the attendant should extend the broken bones, and let the physician set them straight until they are well joined; and apply the dressing and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then place a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And if the break is around the plantar arch of the foot, make a bandage from strips, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken foot; and then bind with a long strip, and let the knot be as large as the palm of the hand, and tie it, as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the break is in the finger, it is necessary that you place a bandage above and another below the finger, so that the hand remains open and straight; then bind the whole hand around, and tighten the ligament between the two [fingers].
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And if the break is in one of the toes, if it is protruding, then set it straight as needed; and bind with the foot, and if you see [it is necessary], place a small straight bandage to raise the break, and do not move it; and if the break is in another toe, such as in the big toe or one of the others, then set it straight, and bind with the healthy toe that follows; or bind them all together, whatever works best, or place a bandage above, as on the big toe; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the abscess, and treat whoever comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 The bones of the thigh are often broken, and it is well seen when it turns front and back; and the restoration is such that one ties a ligament above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant stretches his ligament equally to its part; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ligaments should be towards the knee, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And so if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be near the knee, and let the extension be downward; then let the surgeon place the bone equally with his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply a poultice, and bandage it, if no abscesses form there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 And if there is a hot abscess, let it rest until it subsides, then return to your work and treatment; the plaster is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 And it is necessary that you wrap over the fracture with a bandage, doubled once or twice, leaving the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the nail, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and the ends of the thread should come up; then wrap the bandage over the leg and thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and place one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to evenly distribute the pressure, then begin to bind firmly three or four times over the fracture; and as you go higher on the fracture, bind less; then tie two ends of the thread that you have placed between the leg and the thigh, and bind three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, until you reach near the foot; and bind it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, since no abscess or swelling or other similar thing will occur.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if it happens, then dislocate it, and address what comes there, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that prick, then they must be removed, if possible; and if not possible, then the place must be split, and pull strongly; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that stakes are placed there, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in this restoration the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the thigh is restored in seven days, or a little less or a little more, depending on the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 from the tendon of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 You should know that in the knee joint there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, then it is only a crack or a hole, and it happens in all wounds, whether there is injury or not, and this is felt by everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the healing is such that one puts equal to what is round on its two sides, so that they are assembled as much as possible; then apply the poultice, and place a round bandage if you need it, and bind it as necessary, then follow all the preparations that we have said in other fractures, such as abscesses or others; thus for each incident, apply what is needed until healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	 of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that the leg has II bones, one of which is rightly called "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and all fractures happen in it as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the workings are entirely the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the smaller bone is broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the larger bone is broken, one feels great pain and it can be seen clearly; and it turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction and make it straight and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly and there are several fragments, then the traction should be less and lighter; and align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have completed your work, take two splints of wood that fit the leg on either side, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee down to below; then wrap around it two linen bandages above and below, and tie in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not bend to the right or to the left, and so it is good; and some put a brace along the length of the leg, and it is of wood, and they place the leg in it to prevent movement, and properly done for a fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident; then cure it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle there is no break, but in the bones of the foot there is sometimes breaking and in two places, and nothing happens except breaking in several ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 And if there is breaking in the bones of the foot and you see these bones protruding over each other, place the sick person's foot on the ground as if he wanted to go, and then put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places; then apply a poultice and dressings on top, and place a small board with two flat pegs under the sole of the foot, then bind the foot tightly, and after you have wrapped bandages around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 And when three days or four have passed, release the ligament, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And if there are any broken bones, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and it should be a little wider; then place under the foot the plate that I have mentioned, and tighten it properly. And if there are two or three or more broken bones, place on each bone a splint according to its size, wrapped in a single piece of linen, and place the plate under the foot. And let it stand at the top of the plate above the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 Et tu dois ne pas oublier les autres choses que j'ai dites pour les autres fractures, comme nous l'avons dit auparavant; et soigne chaque incident comme il le faut.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 de la fracture de l'os du poignet
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of the woman's vulva is broken, make her sit with her legs spread apart, then incline her towards the back, and hold her from behind; then fill the woman's vagina with cotton, putting in as much as a fistful; then have the woman stand up and lift her buttocks little by little, and then the cotton will jump until it reaches the entrance of the vulva, and the bone will come back with the fistful; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days or more: then the fracture will be healed, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a reed to its opening, and inflate the entire bladder inside the vagina; then blow strongly into the reed until the bladder is fully inflated inside; this will also heal the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like this for some days, until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the fist of a man is broken, or of a woman, restore it as we have said in the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from one who puts his study and practice into it, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the break, it signifies in many ways the right way of restoration; understand this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three days or less, and it will heal swiftly.
de brisure avec plaie	 of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for one who has a break with wound, especially if it is large, such as the hip bone or shoulder blade or similar, that he be bled immediately, so that the bleeding that we have said proves it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound heals, then seal it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the break in that same hour, or that day, unless an abscess forms there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if an abscess forms there, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would bring about a bad incident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone is visible on the skin, then you must carefully place it between your hands with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if you cannot make equal extensions with your hands, then use this iron instrument which has seven or eight inches in length, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this reason it is necessary for the physician to have three or four, as he needs them for each cure of a break; and let it be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend at all when pressed upon the limb during your work, and let it be pointed at the end, and thicker in the middle, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," for which the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone; and press it once, so that it returns, and both are equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut off the end of the bone so that the instrument can gain purchase on it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument for this purpose, either a knife or scissors; then scrape away what remains in the bone by means of roughness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If it is done so that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not put on the wound any ointment or other thing that has oil, lest it bring about putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the dressing all around, according to the size of the wound, and be well aware that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times have the foolish doctors done this, and have brought upon the patient death or gangrene at other times; and let the constriction be gentler and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or severe, and you fear that an evil accident may happen, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not appropriate to apply bandages; but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two swelling at the wound, remove all that you have put on the wound, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment of theriac and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the swelling runs down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 Et si many days pass, and it cannot heal but rather worsens, know that there are small fragments of bone, for which you must search the wound with a probe, and remove all those loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if an ulcer forms in the place, or another form of corruption, then you must cure it, according to what is said in this preceding chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, as with the thigh or shoulder bones, and other similar large members, do not pull it out, for many times this leads to death, but leave it alone until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 Of bruises that come upon the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 They often come after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Take heed therefore if the wound is fresh: then administer stiptic medicines such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and colocynth, and acacia, and similar others, in whatever quantity you take of these things, or all together, and mix them with stiptic wine or plenty of egg or oil; and place them on the knot in bandages, and bind it well, and do not unbind for many days; and then unbind, and start another, until the swelling is gone; or you can bind on a well-made piece of lead, because the property of lead is that it removes all the swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already hardened like stone, and it must be removed, then shave over it, and expose the excess; or you have it scraped off by some scraper, until it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 Of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the fracture of the bone is healed, and afterward the limb remains weak and fragile, it happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly and not as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or because of very great movements, not at all in their proper time; or because he has little blood in his body, making him weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the treatment is such that you should make the patient eat and soften the body until the blood increases in him; and administer baths and give joy and merriment; then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch draws great nourishment to it, and often bleed it with cold water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and let it return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 of a twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb anew; many foolish physicians have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and possibly death. However, if the nodules and torments are fresh, they must be soaked in hot water, or herbs with softening properties should be boiled, such as leaves of mallow, roots, melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, like dyaquilon well made, and take the juice of mallow, and mix it with lard or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top. Or take ripe figs, and grind them with bran of barley, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is cured by continually and for a long time rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And let there be gentle movement to the member each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the tortuousness is hardened and like stone, and it needs to be removed with an iron, then one should cover it up to the bone with a subtle, light incision; and put caution and care into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When dislocation happens to someone, one must immediately set it back into place without delaying.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Car if one delays, then the place swells, and perhaps one can only barely reset it; therefore, it is not necessary that one move it when it is swollen: often this brings on spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, have the patient fast, then leave them until the abscess subsides; then wash the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as it returns to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 It seldom happens that the jawbones are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is in two ways: either they are slightly separated from their place and somewhat softened; or they are entirely dislocated and hang down towards the chest, and saliva runs out of the mouth so that it cannot be held, nor can the mouth be closed, and it wraps the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must quickly reset it, without delay; and in such a manner that the assistant holds the patient's head, and the healer places his finger from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and let the other two hands be free to maintain balance. And instruct the patient to soften their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the healer should place it evenly until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the returning is difficult, especially if it involves both mandibles together, then bathe them in hot water and oil until you can easily reset them; do not delay the resetting as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are brought back into alignment, and the patient's mouth is closed without softening, place moistened cloths in a cerate made of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind it with soft bands; and let the patient sleep on their back, and keep their eyes between two pillows, so that neither to the right nor to the left is moved, nor does he strain himself to speak, but take light food, as long as the pains are removed, and the jaws are immobilized; and then lightly chew what one wants, and do not struggle to open the mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well immobilized and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two mandibles cannot be reset to their proper place within an hour, and are not converted to their rightful position, then fever and sudden constipation ensue, and perhaps intestinal obstruction, and perhaps pure bile is vomited.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and often he who experiences this dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 from the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The forceps cannot dislocate from the side within the continuity of itself and the hip, but it is sometimes dislocated at the elbow, which is quite evident.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient should lie on his back and extend his arms; then press firmly with your palm, and it will return to its place; then apply a poultice and bandage, and bind it tightly; and the head which is towards the elbow cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates sometimes, reset it to its proper place as we have said; then apply a poultice and bandage, and bind it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until healed; and thus also the shoulder joint is reset when it is displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one is that it dislocates to the lower part of the armpit; and the second is towards the chest; and perhaps it dislocates upwards, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate backwards due to the shoulder, nor inwards due to the nerves. And many times it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially for those who have little flesh, because then it quickly jumps out; for those who have enough flesh, it jumps out with difficulty and goes back with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And perhaps there are some men who have a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 It is therefore necessary for you to examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And the dislocation is known when it descends towards the armpit, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and under the armpit on the back the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it clearly on the back; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the manner is that the minister lifts the hand of the patient high, then places his thumb under it, and lifts the joint forcefully high in place; and the minister lifts the hand, and extends it high, then places it underneath; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in several days after, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and the minister should carefully make a poultice that is softening and soothing, such as a decoction of hollyhock and fenugreek and melilot in water, and apply it; then the patient should be seated on their back, and place under the thumb a pad of cloth equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then the healer places his heel on the pad, and lifts the head of the shoulder vertically, and pulls the hand of the patient; and another minister holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; that shoulder will return immediately, and if you see it this way, then ramain according to this manner: and it is that you make present a man who is larger than the patient; and he should stand straight beside the afflicted side, and push his shoulder under the patient's thumb, and lift the thumb high, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too weak, attach something heavy to them, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And one can also reset it in another way: and take a long log and stick it into the ground so that its tip is as round as a spindle, neither too thick nor too thin; then place it underneath the patient, but with soft drapes on top, and the patient should be standing along the length of the log; then extend his hand downward from the other side like this, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these reasons we have mentioned, perform this cure: take a log that is two arms long and four fingers wide, with a rounded tip so that it can enter deeply underneath the seat, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 Then place the patient's head on the log beneath the drape, so that the log does not strike the patient, then place it under the patient's buttocks; and stretch both arms over the long log, and tie the shoulder above the log, and the arm at the top of the hand, then place the arm on the tread of a wide ladder, and let the hands hang down, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will now be reversed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is in place, however that may be, it is necessary to put under the buttocks an equal ball of wool, then apply the plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and egg white, over all the shoulder and around, then press under the buttocks firmly, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and encircle the hand around its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And it is necessary that he rests for a long time, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal more quickly; and then rest again after V or VII days, and move it; and if it is stiffened and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come into it, or for another reason, then you must apply three cauteries, as stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after VII days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm up, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. 》
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The dislocation that is towards the foot and the breasts, or behind, is done by impact and extension of hands, and another remedy is administered there; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and gradually in movement, then the patient should bathe many times, until that stiffness is relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated by points, and returns by points; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not responded to, because one sees it well and feels it well; and it is dislocated according to each shape. 》
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick person with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 And you must reset it before abscesses form there, because if abscesses form there, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is in the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and is more painful, and death may occur. 》
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 And the reset is like this, when it is such that you can reset it, that with your two hands you extend his hand; and let his arm be spread out, and place the hand of the healthy person around the arm above and below, and push the joint back together at its root, until it returns to its place. 》
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm with the knife that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and let two administrators extend the arm, and hold it with two hands so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from side to side, after you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth around it; and when the patient joins the joint to his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint strongly until it returns; and when it is in place, put on a dry poultice with egg yolk, and hold it firmly, and tie the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then unbind it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	 And if the joint is firmly in its place, loosen the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, then apply the poultice and the ligament again, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels tightness after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is eased; or place on the joint a greasy sheepskin, leave it there for one day and one night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then replace the sheepskin, and have him re-enter the bath; do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see, place on a warm, moist cow dung mixed with butter, and bind it on; thus it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is light, more than other joints However, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the very hour that it is dislocated, lest the place become swollen or develop a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the remedy is such that you place the sick hand on a table, and the attendant extends his hand, and the physician places it evenly, so that he places his palm over the appearance of the joint, and presses until it returns However, you must see if it is well in place; then the patient places the back of his hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the physician places his hand on that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, that is good. If not, then constrain with soothing plasters for these abscesses, and leave it thus without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted; and it does not harm the patient more than while his hand is weakened, and he cannot grasp anything: then know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; there is no other remedy except to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, apply the poultice as we have said, then hold it and leave for V days, then unbind it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it cannot be moved well, and there is some difficulty, then soak it in hot water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated in each part, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the front; then stretch the finger, and push the dislocation towards your fingertips until it returns to its place, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the side where it is dislocated; and leave it for II days, then bind it again that day; and bind it as we have said, and unbind it after a day, and make it move, and rebind it; and do this often, until it is straightened, and do the same if it is dislocated at the front of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 About the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are several dislocations, there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the sign of this is that the excrement leaps out without control, and he cannot hold it in, and often some members are paralyzed, either both thighs or both arms or one, and often the spine moves into four parts; the one that moves to the back is called "gibbosity": the cure for this is that you return if the gibbosity comes from childhood: then there is no cure or healing of all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancients describe cures with great words, where there is not much benefit in all of them; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the condition called "gilbositeit" which affects the chest in front, there is neither intelligence nor health; and likewise that which comes directly on two sides, and it cannot be cured except by that which properly affects the back, as I say; and it is that the patient should be stretched out on his back in one equal place, and have restraint underneath him so that he does not injure himself; then drive a log into the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a rope underneath the saddle of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants should know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two logs; and let them be well secured, the logs as we have said, and the doctor should place his palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return with this cure, then take a board of three arms in length, and place it under the patient, and let the patient be on his side, and push the head of the board under the patient, then put the middle of the board on the spine; and let the physician put his feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same with the arm that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you fix two stakes at the head of the patient with an arm's length apart, and towards the feet two others, and there be between each stake a palm's length apart in length; and let there be in each stake one hole, where the arm passes through, and the stakes should be firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each of the two stakes there should be a turning stake on which the rope turns, and between the two turning stakes there should be two small stakes of a palm's length to turn the arm; and then tie the rope that is among the seats to the arm towards the head, and the other rope to the other arm towards the feet, and each of the assistants turns his arm all along the rope, and the master sets the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is equal, put a desiccating poultice with plenty of egg, and then the dressing, and then the bandage of a tablet three fingers long, which should cover the place of the yellowness and the part of the healthy spine, then bind with a cord, as we have said, and let the patient use delicate nourishment until he is healed; and if anything happens at the end of the healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the bandage that we have mentioned before; sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back spine of the back, and one thinks it is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, because of which one should not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 Of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Know that in the joints of the hip and the shoulder, dislocations occur alone, not like other joints. The joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and it is more commonly dislocated inside than elsewhere, and rarely in front or behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the sign of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick person's knee opens more than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend his knee at all; and the place which is near is swollen with an abscess, hot, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the sign of that which comes to lack, is that this event is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 And the sign of that which comes to the front, is that he straightens his leg according to the completion; nevertheless, do not bend the knee with pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot move forward, and he retains his urine, and his throat swells, and when he walks, he steps on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the sign of that which comes to the back, is that he cannot expand his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the throat is softened, and the head of the thigh is in the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 The remedies for this type of dislocation are such that if the dislocation is old, it remains according to its nature, and there is no treatment for it; nor should one have any expectation for it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.
